   <h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading">Suriname</h1> 
   <div id="bodyContent" class="vector-body"> 
    <div id="siteSub" class="noprint">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div> 
    <div id="contentSub"></div> 
    <div id="contentSub2"></div> 
    <div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a> 
    <div id="mw-content-text" class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" lang="en" dir="ltr">
     <div class="mw-parser-output">
      <div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">
       Country in South America
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       "Surinam" redirects here. For the former English colony, see <a href="/wiki/Surinam_(English_colony)" title="Surinam (English colony)">Surinam (English colony)</a>. For the former Dutch colony, see <a href="/wiki/Surinam_(Dutch_colony)" title="Surinam (Dutch colony)">Surinam (Dutch colony)</a>. For the constituent country in the Kingdom of the Netherlands, see <a href="/wiki/Suriname_(Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands)" title="Suriname (Kingdom of the Netherlands)">Suriname (Kingdom of the Netherlands)</a>. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Suriname_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Suriname (disambiguation)">Suriname (disambiguation)</a>.
      </div>

            <li>13.7% <a href="/wiki/Javanese_Surinamese" title="Javanese Surinamese">Javanese</a></li>
            <li>13.4% <a href="/wiki/Multiracial" class="mw-redirect" title="Multiracial">Other Mixed</a><br><span style="font-size:85%;">(incl. <a href="/wiki/Dougla" class="mw-redirect" title="Dougla">Douglas</a>)</span></li>

            <li>1% <a href="/wiki/White_Surinamese" title="White Surinamese">European</a></li>

      <p><b>Suriname</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/sj/: 's' in 'consume'">sj</span><span title="/ʊər/: 'our' in 'tour'">ʊər</span><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span></span>,<span class="wrap"> </span>-<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/ɑː/: 'a' in 'father'">ɑː</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span></span>/</a></span></span>) or <b>Surinam</b>, officially known as the <b>Republic of Suriname</b> (<a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>: <i lang="nl">Republiek Suriname</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Dutch" title="Help:IPA/Dutch">[reːpyˌblik ˌsyːriˈnaːmə]</a></span>), is a country on the northeastern <a href="/wiki/Atlantic" class="mw-redirect" title="Atlantic">Atlantic</a> coast of <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a>. <a href="/wiki/Borders_of_Suriname" title="Borders of Suriname">It is bordered</a> by the Atlantic Ocean to the north, <a href="/wiki/French_Guiana" title="French Guiana">French Guiana</a> to the east, <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a> to the west and <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> to the south. At just under 165,000 square kilometers (64,000 square miles), it is the smallest <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign state</a> in South America.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">[note 1]</a></sup> Suriname has a population of approximately 575,990,<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-8">[8]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2019_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP_2019-9">[9]</a></sup> most of whom live on the country's north coast, in and around the capital and largest city, <a href="/wiki/Paramaribo" title="Paramaribo">Paramaribo</a>. </p>
      <p>Situated slightly north of the <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">Equator</a>, Suriname is a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_country" class="mw-redirect" title="Tropical country">tropical country</a> dominated by rain forests. Its extensive tree cover is vital to the country's efforts to <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_in_Suriname" title="Climate change in Suriname">mitigate climate change</a> and maintain <a href="/wiki/Carbon_negativity" class="mw-redirect" title="Carbon negativity">carbon negativity</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[note 2]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country">developing country</a> with a <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">high level of human development</a>, <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Suriname" title="Economy of Suriname">Suriname's economy</a> is heavily dependent on its abundant natural resources, namely bauxite, gold, petroleum and agricultural products. </p>
      <p>Suriname was inhabited as early as the fourth millennium BC by various indigenous peoples, including the Arawaks, Caribs, and Wayana. Europeans arrived in the 16th century, with the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">Dutch</a> establishing control over much of the country's current territory by the late 17th century. During the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Surinam" class="mw-redirect" title="Dutch Surinam">Dutch colonial period</a>, Suriname was a lucrative source of <a href="/wiki/Sugar" title="Sugar">sugar</a>, its <a href="/wiki/Plantation_economy" title="Plantation economy">plantation economy</a> driven by African slave labor and, after abolition of slavery in 1863, <a href="/wiki/Indentured_servitude" title="Indentured servitude">indentured servants</a> from Asia. In 1954, Suriname became one of the <a href="/wiki/Constituent_state" title="Constituent state">constituent countries</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands" title="Kingdom of the Netherlands">Kingdom of the Netherlands</a>. On 25 November 1975, <a href="/wiki/Suriname_(Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands)" title="Suriname (Kingdom of the Netherlands)">Suriname</a> left the Kingdom to become an <a href="/wiki/Independence" title="Independence">independent</a> state, but continues to maintain close economic, diplomatic, and cultural ties. </p>
      <p>Suriname is considered to be a culturally <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> country, and is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Community" title="Caribbean Community">Caribbean Community</a> (CARICOM). Suriname is the only sovereign nation outside of Europe where <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a> is the official and prevailing language of government, business, media, and education.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-16">[14]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sranan_Tongo" title="Sranan Tongo">Sranan Tongo</a>, an English-based <a href="/wiki/English_creole" class="mw-redirect" title="English creole">creole language</a>, is a widely used <i><a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">lingua franca</a></i>. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suriname&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>The name <i>Suriname</i> may derive from an indigenous people called <i>Surinen,</i> who inhabited the area at the time of European contact.<sup id="cite_ref-Britannica_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-17">[15]</a></sup> The suffix -ame, common in Surinamese river and place names (see also the <a href="/wiki/Coppename_River" title="Coppename River">Coppename River</a>), may come from <i>aima</i> or <i>eima</i>, meaning river or creek mouth, in <a href="/wiki/Lokono_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Lokono language">Lokono</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Arawak_language" title="Arawak language">Arawak language</a> spoken in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[16]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The earliest European sources give variants of "Suriname" as the name of the <a href="/wiki/Suriname_River" title="Suriname River">river</a> on which colonies were eventually founded. <a href="/wiki/Lawrence_Kemys" title="Lawrence Kemys">Lawrence Kemys</a> wrote in his <i>Relation of the Second Voyage to Guiana</i> of passing a river called "<i>Shurinama</i>" as he travelled along the coast. In 1598, a fleet of three Dutch ships visiting the Wild Coast mention passing the river "<i>Surinamo</i>". In 1617, a Dutch notary spelled the name of the river on which a Dutch trading post had existed three years earlier as "<i>Surrenant</i>".<sup id="cite_ref-De_Naam_Suriname_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-De_Naam_Suriname-19">[17]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>British settlers, who in 1630 founded the first European colony at Marshall's Creek along the Suriname River, spelled the name as "<i>Surinam</i>"; this would long remain the standard spelling in English.<sup id="cite_ref-Marshall_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marshall-20">[18]</a></sup> The Dutch navigator <a href="/wiki/David_Pietersz._de_Vries" title="David Pietersz. de Vries">David Pietersz. de Vries</a> wrote of traveling up the "<i>Sername</i>" river in 1634 until he encountered the English colony there; the terminal vowel remained in future Dutch spellings and pronunciations. In 1640, a Spanish manuscript entitled "General Description of All His Majesty's Dominions in America" called the river "<i>Soronama</i>". In 1653, instructions given to a British fleet sailing to meet <a href="/wiki/Francis_Willoughby,_5th_Baron_Willoughby_of_Parham" title="Francis Willoughby, 5th Baron Willoughby of Parham">Lord Willoughby</a> in <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a>, which at the time was the seat of English colonial government in the region, again spelled the name of the colony "<i>Surinam</i>". A 1663 royal charter said the region around the river was "called Serrinam also Surrinam".<sup id="cite_ref-De_Naam_Suriname_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-De_Naam_Suriname-19">[17]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As a result of the "<i>Surrinam</i>" spelling, 19th-century British sources offered the folk etymology "<i>Surryham</i>", saying it was the name given to the Suriname River by Lord Willoughby in the 1660s in honour of the <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Howard,_5th_Duke_of_Norfolk" title="Thomas Howard, 5th Duke of Norfolk">Duke of Norfolk and Earl of Surrey</a> when an English <a href="/wiki/Surinam_(English_colony)" title="Surinam (English colony)">colony</a> was established under a grant from King <a href="/wiki/Charles_II_of_England" title="Charles II of England">Charles II</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-De_Naam_Suriname_19-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-De_Naam_Suriname-19">[17]</a></sup> This folk etymology can be found repeated in later English-language sources.<sup id="cite_ref-International_Boundaries:_A_Case_Study_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-International_Boundaries:_A_Case_Study-21">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-United_Services_Magazine_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-United_Services_Magazine-22">[20]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>When the territory was taken over by the Dutch, it became part of a group of colonies known as <a href="/wiki/Dutch_colonization_of_the_Guianas" class="mw-redirect" title="Dutch colonization of the Guianas">Dutch Guiana</a>. The official spelling of the country's English name was changed from "Surinam" to "Suriname" in January 1978, but "Surinam" can still be found in English, such as Suriname's national airline <a href="/wiki/Surinam_Airways" title="Surinam Airways">Surinam Airways</a>. The older English name is reflected in the English pronunciation, <span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="/sj/: 's' in 'consume'">sj</span><span title="/ʊər/: 'our' in 'tour'">ʊər</span><span title="/ɪ/: 'i' in 'kit'">ɪ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span></span>,<span class="wrap"> </span>-<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/ɑː/: 'a' in 'father'">ɑː</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span></span>/</a></span></span>. In <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>, the official language of Suriname, the pronunciation is <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Dutch" title="Help:IPA/Dutch">[ˌsyriˈnaːmə]</a></span>, with the main stress on the third syllable and a <a href="/wiki/Schwa" title="Schwa">schwa</a> terminal vowel. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suriname&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Maroon_village,_Suriname_River,_1955.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Maroon_village%2C_Suriname_River%2C_1955.jpg/220px-Maroon_village%2C_Suriname_River%2C_1955.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Maroon_village%2C_Suriname_River%2C_1955.jpg/330px-Maroon_village%2C_Suriname_River%2C_1955.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Maroon_village%2C_Suriname_River%2C_1955.jpg/440px-Maroon_village%2C_Suriname_River%2C_1955.jpg 2x" data-file-width="652" data-file-height="444"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Maroon_village,_Suriname_River,_1955.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Maroon village, along <a href="/wiki/Suriname_River" title="Suriname River">Suriname River</a>, 1955
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Suriname" title="History of Suriname">History of Suriname</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Indigenous settlement of Suriname dates back to 3,000 BC. The largest tribes were the <a href="/wiki/Arawak" title="Arawak">Arawak</a>, a nomadic coastal tribe that lived from hunting and fishing. They were the first inhabitants in the area. The <a href="/wiki/Kalina_people" title="Kalina people">Carib</a> also settled in the area and conquered the Arawak by using their superior sailing ships. They settled in Galibi (<i>Kupali Yumï,</i> meaning "tree of the forefathers") at the mouth of the <a href="/wiki/Marowijne_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Marowijne River">Marowijne River</a>. While the larger Arawak and Carib tribes lived along the coast and savanna, smaller groups of indigenous people lived in the inland rainforest, such as the <a href="/wiki/Akurio" class="mw-redirect" title="Akurio">Akurio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tri%C3%B3" class="mw-redirect" title="Trió">Trió</a>, <a href="/wiki/Warrau" class="mw-redirect" title="Warrau">Warrau</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wayana" title="Wayana">Wayana</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colonial_period">Colonial period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suriname&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Colonial period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Presidential_palace,_Paramaribo,_Suriname.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Presidential_palace%2C_Paramaribo%2C_Suriname.jpg/220px-Presidential_palace%2C_Paramaribo%2C_Suriname.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Presidential_palace%2C_Paramaribo%2C_Suriname.jpg/330px-Presidential_palace%2C_Paramaribo%2C_Suriname.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Presidential_palace%2C_Paramaribo%2C_Suriname.jpg/440px-Presidential_palace%2C_Paramaribo%2C_Suriname.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="375"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Presidential_palace,_Paramaribo,_Suriname.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Presidential_Palace_of_Suriname" title="Presidential Palace of Suriname">Presidential Palace of Suriname</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Surinam_(English_colony)" title="Surinam (English colony)">Surinam (English colony)</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Surinam_(Dutch_colony)" title="Surinam (Dutch colony)">Surinam (Dutch colony)</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Beginning in the 16th century, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_France" title="Kingdom of France">French</a>, <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_Spain" title="Habsburg Spain">Spanish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">English</a> explorers visited the area. A century later, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Republic" title="Dutch Republic">Dutch</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">English</a> settlers established <a href="/wiki/Plantation" title="Plantation">plantation</a> colonies along the many rivers in the fertile Guiana plains. The earliest documented colony in <a href="/wiki/The_Guianas" title="The Guianas">Guiana</a> was an English settlement named Marshall's Creek along the Suriname River.<sup id="cite_ref-Marshall_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Marshall-20">[18]</a></sup> After that there was another short-lived English colony called <a href="/wiki/Surinam_(English_colony)" title="Surinam (English colony)">Surinam</a> that lasted from 1650 to 1667. </p>
      <p>Disputes arose between the Dutch and the English for control of this territory. In 1667, during negotiations leading to the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Breda_(1667)" title="Treaty of Breda (1667)">Treaty of Breda</a> after the <a href="/wiki/Second_Anglo-Dutch_War" title="Second Anglo-Dutch War">Second Anglo-Dutch War</a>, the Dutch decided to keep the nascent plantation colony of Surinam they had gained from the English. In return the English kept <a href="/wiki/New_Amsterdam" title="New Amsterdam">New Amsterdam</a>, the main city of the former colony of <a href="/wiki/New_Netherland" title="New Netherland">New Netherland</a> in North America on the mid-Atlantic coast. The British renamed it after the Duke of York: <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>. </p>
      <p>In 1683, the <a href="/wiki/Society_of_Suriname" title="Society of Suriname">Society of Suriname</a> was founded by the city of <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Cornelis_van_Aerssen_van_Sommelsdijck" title="Cornelis van Aerssen van Sommelsdijck">Van Aerssen van Sommelsdijck</a> family, and the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_West_India_Company" title="Dutch West India Company">Dutch West India Company</a>. The society was chartered to manage and defend the colony. The planters of the colony relied heavily on <a href="/wiki/Slavery_in_Africa" title="Slavery in Africa">African slaves</a> to cultivate, harvest and process the commodity crops of coffee, cocoa, sugar cane and cotton plantations along the rivers. Planters' treatment of the slaves was notoriously brutal even by the standards of the time<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[21]</a></sup>—historian <a href="/wiki/C._R._Boxer" title="C. R. Boxer">C. R. Boxer</a> wrote that "man's inhumanity to man just about reached its limits in Surinam"<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[22]</a></sup>—and many slaves escaped the plantations. In November 1795, the Society was nationalized by the <a href="/wiki/Batavian_Republic" title="Batavian Republic">Batavian Republic</a> and from then on, the Batavian Republic and its legal successors (the Kingdom of Holland and the Kingdom of the Netherlands) governed the territory as a national colony, barring a period of British occupation between 1799 and 1802, and between 1804 and 1816. </p>
      <p>With the help of the <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">native South Americans</a> living in the adjoining rain forests, these runaway slaves established a new and unique culture in the interior that was highly successful in its own right. They were known collectively in English as <a href="/wiki/Maroon_(people)" class="mw-redirect" title="Maroon (people)">Maroons</a>, in French as <i>Nèg'Marrons</i> (literally meaning "brown negroes", that is "pale-skinned negroes"), and in Dutch as <i>Marrons.</i> The Maroons gradually developed several independent tribes through a process of <a href="/wiki/Ethnogenesis" title="Ethnogenesis">ethnogenesis</a>, as they were made up of slaves from different African ethnicities. These tribes include the <a href="/wiki/Saramaka" title="Saramaka">Saramaka</a>, Paramaka, <a href="/wiki/Ndyuka_people" title="Ndyuka people">Ndyuka</a> or Aukan, <a href="/wiki/Kwinti" class="mw-redirect" title="Kwinti">Kwinti</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aluku" title="Aluku">Aluku</a> or Boni, and Matawai. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Water-front_houses_in_Paramaribo,_1955.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Water-front_houses_in_Paramaribo%2C_1955.jpg/220px-Water-front_houses_in_Paramaribo%2C_1955.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="228" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Water-front_houses_in_Paramaribo%2C_1955.jpg/330px-Water-front_houses_in_Paramaribo%2C_1955.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Water-front_houses_in_Paramaribo%2C_1955.jpg/440px-Water-front_houses_in_Paramaribo%2C_1955.jpg 2x" data-file-width="671" data-file-height="694"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Water-front_houses_in_Paramaribo,_1955.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Waterfront houses in <a href="/wiki/Paramaribo" title="Paramaribo">Paramaribo</a>, 1955
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Maroons often raided plantations to recruit new members from the slaves and capture women, as well as to acquire weapons, food and supplies. They sometimes killed planters and their families in the raids; colonists built defenses, which were significant enough that they were shown on 18th-century maps.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[23]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The colonists also mounted armed campaigns against the Maroons, who generally escaped through the rain forest, which they knew much better than did the colonists. To end hostilities, in the 18th century the European colonial authorities signed several peace treaties with different tribes. They granted the Maroons sovereign status and trade rights in their inland territories, giving them autonomy. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Abolition_of_slavery">Abolition of slavery</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suriname&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Abolition of slavery">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Suriname" title="Human rights in Suriname">Human rights in Suriname</a>
      </div> 
      <p>From 1861 to 1863, with the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a> underway, and enslaved people escaping to Northern territory controlled by the <a href="/wiki/Union_(American_Civil_War)" title="Union (American Civil War)">Union</a>, United States President <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Lincoln" title="Abraham Lincoln">Abraham Lincoln</a> and <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_Abraham_Lincoln" title="Presidency of Abraham Lincoln">his administration</a> looked abroad for places to relocate people who were freed from enslavement and who wanted to leave the United States. It opened negotiations with the Dutch government regarding African-American emigration to and colonization of the <a href="/wiki/Surinam_(Dutch_colony)" title="Surinam (Dutch colony)">Dutch colony of Suriname</a>. Nothing came of the idea, and the idea was dropped after 1864.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[24]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Netherlands abolished slavery in Suriname in 1863, under a gradual process that required enslaved people to work on plantations for 10 transition years for minimal pay, which was considered as partial compensation for their masters. After that transition period expired in 1873, most <a href="/wiki/Freedmen" class="mw-redirect" title="Freedmen">freedmen</a> largely abandoned the plantations where they had worked for several generations in favor of the capital city, <a href="/wiki/Paramaribo" title="Paramaribo">Paramaribo</a>. Some of them were able to purchase the plantations they worked on, especially in the district of Para and Coronie. Their descendants still live on those grounds today. Several plantation owners did not pay their former enslaved workers the pay they owed them for the ten years following 1863. They paid the workers with the property rights of the ground of the plantation in order to escape their debt to the workers.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[25]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Suriname_immigranten_afkomstig_uit_Nederlands-Indi%C3%AB_de_vrouw_rechts_draagt_een_peniti_tak_broche_TMnr_60008927.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Suriname_immigranten_afkomstig_uit_Nederlands-Indi%C3%AB_de_vrouw_rechts_draagt_een_peniti_tak_broche_TMnr_60008927.jpg/220px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Suriname_immigranten_afkomstig_uit_Nederlands-Indi%C3%AB_de_vrouw_rechts_draagt_een_peniti_tak_broche_TMnr_60008927.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Suriname_immigranten_afkomstig_uit_Nederlands-Indi%C3%AB_de_vrouw_rechts_draagt_een_peniti_tak_broche_TMnr_60008927.jpg/330px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Suriname_immigranten_afkomstig_uit_Nederlands-Indi%C3%AB_de_vrouw_rechts_draagt_een_peniti_tak_broche_TMnr_60008927.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Suriname_immigranten_afkomstig_uit_Nederlands-Indi%C3%AB_de_vrouw_rechts_draagt_een_peniti_tak_broche_TMnr_60008927.jpg/440px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Suriname_immigranten_afkomstig_uit_Nederlands-Indi%C3%AB_de_vrouw_rechts_draagt_een_peniti_tak_broche_TMnr_60008927.jpg 2x" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="548"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Suriname_immigranten_afkomstig_uit_Nederlands-Indi%C3%AB_de_vrouw_rechts_draagt_een_peniti_tak_broche_TMnr_60008927.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Javanese_people" title="Javanese people">Javanese</a> immigrants brought as contract workers from the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_Indies" title="Dutch East Indies">Dutch East Indies</a>. Picture was taken between 1880 and 1900.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>As a plantation colony, Suriname had an economy dependent on labor-intensive commodity crops. To make up for a shortage of labor, the Dutch recruited and transported contract or <a href="/wiki/Indentured_laborer" class="mw-redirect" title="Indentured laborer">indentured laborers</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_Indies" title="Dutch East Indies">Dutch East Indies</a> (modern <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>) and <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> (the latter through an arrangement with the British, who then ruled the area). In addition, during the late 19th and early 20th centuries, small numbers of laborers, mostly men, were recruited from China and the Middle East. </p>
      <p>Although Suriname's population remains relatively small, because of this complex colonization and exploitation, it is one of the most ethnically and culturally diverse countries in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[26]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[27]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Decolonization">Decolonization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suriname&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Decolonization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Decolonization_of_the_Americas" title="Decolonization of the Americas">Decolonization of the Americas</a>
      </div> 
      <p>During <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, on 23 November 1941, under an agreement with the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_government-in-exile" title="Dutch government-in-exile">Netherlands government-in-exile</a>, the United States occupied Suriname to protect the <a href="/wiki/Bauxite" title="Bauxite">bauxite</a> mines to support the Allies' war effort.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[28]</a></sup> In 1942, the Dutch government-in-exile began to review the relations between the Netherlands and its colonies in terms of the post-war period. </p>
      <p>In 1954, Suriname became one of the constituent countries of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands" title="Kingdom of the Netherlands">Kingdom of the Netherlands</a>, along with the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_Antilles" title="Netherlands Antilles">Netherlands Antilles</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>. In this construction, the Netherlands retained control of its defense and foreign affairs. In 1974, the local government, led by the <a href="/wiki/National_Party_of_Suriname" title="National Party of Suriname">National Party of Suriname</a> (NPS) (whose membership was largely <a href="/wiki/Creole_peoples" title="Creole peoples">Creole</a>, meaning ethnically African or mixed African-European) started negotiations with the Dutch government leading towards full independence, which was granted on 25 November 1975. A large part of Suriname's economy for the first decade following independence was fueled by foreign aid provided by the Dutch government. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence">Independence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suriname&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Independence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Henck_Arron,_Beatrix,_Johan_Ferrier_1975.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Henck_Arron%2C_Beatrix%2C_Johan_Ferrier_1975.jpg/220px-Henck_Arron%2C_Beatrix%2C_Johan_Ferrier_1975.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Henck_Arron%2C_Beatrix%2C_Johan_Ferrier_1975.jpg/330px-Henck_Arron%2C_Beatrix%2C_Johan_Ferrier_1975.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Henck_Arron%2C_Beatrix%2C_Johan_Ferrier_1975.jpg/440px-Henck_Arron%2C_Beatrix%2C_Johan_Ferrier_1975.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2016" data-file-height="2016"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Henck_Arron,_Beatrix,_Johan_Ferrier_1975.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Henck_Arron" title="Henck Arron">Henck Arron</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beatrix_of_the_Netherlands" title="Beatrix of the Netherlands">Beatrix</a> and <a href="/wiki/Johan_Ferrier" title="Johan Ferrier">Johan Ferrier</a> on 25 November 1975
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The first President of the country was <a href="/wiki/Johan_Ferrier" title="Johan Ferrier">Johan Ferrier</a>, the former governor, with <a href="/wiki/Henck_Arron" title="Henck Arron">Henck Arron</a> (the then leader of the NPS) as Prime Minister. In the years leading up to independence, nearly one-third of the population of Suriname emigrated to the Netherlands, amidst concern that the new country would fare worse under independence than it had as a constituent country of the Kingdom of the Netherlands. Surinamese politics did degenerate into ethnic polarisation and corruption soon after independence, with the NPS using Dutch aid money for partisan purposes. Its leaders were accused of fraud in the <a href="/wiki/1977_Surinamese_general_election" title="1977 Surinamese general election">1977 elections</a>, in which Arron won a further term, and the discontent was such that a large portion<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (August 2020)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> of the population fled to the Netherlands, joining the already significant Surinamese community there.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[29]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1980_military_coup">1980 military coup</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suriname&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 1980 military coup">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/1980_Surinamese_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1980 Surinamese coup d'état">1980 Surinamese coup d'état</a>
      </div> 
      <p>On 25 February 1980, a <a href="/wiki/1980_Surinamese_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="1980 Surinamese coup d'état">military coup</a> overthrew Arron's government. It was initiated by a group of 16 sergeants, led by <a href="/wiki/D%C3%A9si_Bouterse" title="Dési Bouterse">Dési Bouterse</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-16">[14]</a></sup> Opponents of the military regime attempted counter-coups in April 1980, August 1980, 15 March 1981, and again on 12 March 1982. The first counter attempt was led by <a href="/wiki/Fred_Ormskerk" title="Fred Ormskerk">Fred Ormskerk</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Janssen2011_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Janssen2011-32">[30]</a></sup> the second by <a href="/wiki/Marxism%E2%80%93Leninism" title="Marxism–Leninism">Marxist-Leninists</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[31]</a></sup> the third by <a href="/wiki/Wilfred_Hawker" title="Wilfred Hawker">Wilfred Hawker</a>, and the fourth by <a href="/wiki/Surendre_Rambocus" title="Surendre Rambocus">Surendre Rambocus</a>. </p>
      <p>Hawker escaped from prison during the fourth counter-coup attempt, but he was captured and summarily executed. Between 2&nbsp;am and 5&nbsp;am on 7 December 1982, the military, under the leadership of Dési Bouterse, rounded up 13 prominent citizens who had criticized the military dictatorship and held them at <a href="/wiki/Fort_Zeelandia_(Paramaribo)" title="Fort Zeelandia (Paramaribo)">Fort Zeelandia</a> in Paramaribo.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[32]</a></sup> The dictatorship had all these men <a href="/wiki/December_murders" title="December murders">executed over the next three days</a>, along with Rambocus and <a href="/wiki/Jiwansingh_Sheombar" class="mw-redirect" title="Jiwansingh Sheombar">Jiwansingh Sheombar</a> (who was also involved in the fourth counter-coup attempt). </p> 
      <h3><span id="Civil_war.2C_elections.2C_and_constitution"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Civil_war,_elections,_and_constitution">Civil war, elections, and constitution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suriname&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Civil war, elections, and constitution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The brutal <a href="/wiki/Suriname_Guerrilla_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Suriname Guerrilla War">civil war between the Suriname army and Maroons</a> loyal to rebel leader <a href="/wiki/Ronnie_Brunswijk" title="Ronnie Brunswijk">Ronnie Brunswijk</a>, begun in 1986, continued and its effects further weakened Bouterse's position during the 1990s. Due to the civil war, more than 10,000 Surinamese, mostly Maroons, fled to <a href="/wiki/French_Guiana" title="French Guiana">French Guiana</a> in the late 1980s.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[33]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>National elections were held in 1987. The National Assembly adopted a new constitution that allowed Bouterse to remain in charge of the army. Dissatisfied with the government, Bouterse summarily dismissed the ministers in 1990, by telephone. This event became popularly known as the "Telephone Coup". His power began to wane after the 1991 elections. </p>
      <p>In 1999, the Netherlands tried Bouterse <i>in absentia</i> on drug smuggling charges. He was <a href="/wiki/Trial_in_absentia" title="Trial in absentia">convicted</a> and sentenced to prison but remained in Suriname.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[34]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/1999_Surinamese_protests" title="1999 Surinamese protests">1999 Surinamese protests</a> occurred in 1999. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="21st_century">21st century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suriname&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 21st century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>On 19 July 2010, the former dictator <a href="/wiki/D%C3%A9si_Bouterse" title="Dési Bouterse">Dési Bouterse</a> returned to power when he was elected as the president of Suriname.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[35]</a></sup> Before his election in 2010, he, along with 24 others, had been charged with the murders of 15 prominent dissidents in the December murders. However, in 2012, two months before the verdict in the trial, the National Assembly extended its <a href="/wiki/Amnesty" title="Amnesty">amnesty</a> law and provided Bouterse and the others with amnesty of these charges. He was reelected on 14 July 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[36]</a></sup> However, Bouterse was convicted by a Surinamese court on 29 November 2019 and given a 20-year sentence for his role in the 1982 killings.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[37]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>After winning the <a href="/wiki/2020_Surinamese_general_election" title="2020 Surinamese general election">2020 elections</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[38]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Chan_Santokhi" title="Chan Santokhi">Chan Santokhi</a> was the sole nomination for <a href="/wiki/President_of_Suriname" title="President of Suriname">president of Suriname</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[39]</a></sup> On 13 July, Santokhi was elected president by acclamation in an <a href="/wiki/Uncontested_election" title="Uncontested election">uncontested election</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[40]</a></sup> He was inaugurated on 16 July in a ceremony without public attendance due to the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic_in_Suriname" title="COVID-19 pandemic in Suriname">COVID-19 pandemic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[41]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suriname&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:AssembleeSurinaam.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/AssembleeSurinaam.jpg/220px-AssembleeSurinaam.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="168" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/AssembleeSurinaam.jpg/330px-AssembleeSurinaam.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/AssembleeSurinaam.jpg/440px-AssembleeSurinaam.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2499" data-file-height="1905"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:AssembleeSurinaam.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>National Assembly
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Paramaribo,_Hof_van_Justitie_(Court_of_Justice).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Paramaribo%2C_Hof_van_Justitie_%28Court_of_Justice%29.jpg/220px-Paramaribo%2C_Hof_van_Justitie_%28Court_of_Justice%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Paramaribo%2C_Hof_van_Justitie_%28Court_of_Justice%29.jpg/330px-Paramaribo%2C_Hof_van_Justitie_%28Court_of_Justice%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Paramaribo%2C_Hof_van_Justitie_%28Court_of_Justice%29.jpg/440px-Paramaribo%2C_Hof_van_Justitie_%28Court_of_Justice%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Paramaribo,_Hof_van_Justitie_(Court_of_Justice).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Court of Justice
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Suriname" title="Politics of Suriname">Politics of Suriname</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The Republic of Suriname is a <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative democratic</a> republic, based on the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Suriname" title="Constitution of Suriname">Constitution of 1987</a>. The legislative branch of government consists of a 51-member <a href="/wiki/Unicameral" class="mw-redirect" title="Unicameral">unicameral</a> <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Suriname" class="mw-redirect" title="National Assembly of Suriname">National Assembly</a>, simultaneously and popularly elected for a five-year term. </p>
      <p>In the elections held on Tuesday, 25 May 2010, the <i>Megacombinatie</i> won 23 of the National Assembly seats followed by <i>Nationale Front</i> with 20 seats. A much smaller number, important for coalition-building, went to the "A‑combinatie" and to the <i>Volksalliantie.</i> The parties held negotiations to form coalitions. Elections were held on 25 May 2015, and the National Assembly again elected Desire Bouterse as president.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[42]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/President_of_Suriname" title="President of Suriname">president of Suriname</a> is elected for a five-year term by a two-thirds majority of the National Assembly. If at least two-thirds of the National Assembly cannot agree to vote for one presidential candidate, a People's Assembly is formed from all National Assembly delegates and regional and municipal representatives who were elected by popular vote in the most recent national election. The president may be elected by a majority of the People's Assembly called for the special election. </p>
      <p>As head of government, the president appoints a sixteen-minister cabinet. A vice president is normally elected for a five-year term at the same time as the president, by a simple majority in the National Assembly or People's Assembly. There is no constitutional provision for removal or replacement of the president, except in the case of resignation. </p>
      <p>The judiciary is headed by the <a href="/wiki/High_Court_of_Justice_of_Suriname" title="High Court of Justice of Suriname">High Court of Justice of Suriname</a> (Supreme Court). This court supervises the magistrate courts. Members are appointed for life by the president in consultation with the National Assembly, the State Advisory Council, and the National Order of Private Attorneys. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suriname&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Suriname" title="Foreign relations of Suriname">Foreign relations of Suriname</a>
      </div> 
      <p>President Dési Bouterse was convicted and sentenced in the Netherlands to 11 years of imprisonment for drug trafficking. He is the main suspect in the court case concerning the December murders, the 1982 assassination of opponents of military rule in <a href="/wiki/Fort_Zeelandia_(Paramaribo)" title="Fort Zeelandia (Paramaribo)">Fort Zeelandia</a>, Paramaribo. These two cases still strain relations between the Netherlands and Suriname.<sup id="cite_ref-minbuza_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-minbuza-45">[43]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Due to Suriname's Dutch colonial history, Suriname had a long-standing special relationship with the Netherlands. The Dutch government has stated that it will maintain limited contact with the president.<sup id="cite_ref-minbuza_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-minbuza-45">[43]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Bouterse was elected as president of Suriname in 2010. The Netherlands in July 2014 dropped Suriname as a member of its development program.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[44]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Since 1991, the United States has maintained positive relations with Suriname. The two countries work together through the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Caribbean_Basin_Security_Initiative&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Caribbean Basin Security Initiative (page does not exist)">Caribbean Basin Security Initiative</a> (CBSI) and the U.S. President's Emergency Plan for AIDS Relief (PEPFAR). Suriname also receives military funding from the U.S. Department of Defense.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[45]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> relations and cooperation with Suriname are carried out both on a bilateral and a regional basis. There are ongoing EU-<a href="/wiki/Community_of_Latin_American_and_Caribbean_States" title="Community of Latin American and Caribbean States">Community of Latin American and Caribbean States</a> (CELAC) and EU-<a href="/wiki/CARIFORUM" title="CARIFORUM">CARIFORUM</a> dialogues. Suriname is party to the <a href="/wiki/Cotonou_Agreement" title="Cotonou Agreement">Cotonou Agreement</a>, the partnership agreement among the members of the African, Caribbean and Pacific Group of States and the European Union.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[46]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 17 February 2005, the leaders of <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a> and Suriname signed the "Agreement for the deepening of bilateral cooperation between the Government of Barbados and the Government of the Republic of Suriname."<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[47]</a></sup> On 23–24 April 2009, both nations formed a Joint Commission in <a href="/wiki/Paramaribo" title="Paramaribo">Paramaribo</a>, Suriname, to improve relations and to expand into various areas of cooperation.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[48]</a></sup> They held a second meeting toward this goal on 3–4 March 2011, in Dover, Barbados. Their representatives reviewed issues of agriculture, trade, investment, as well as international transport.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[49]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the late 2000s, Suriname intensified development cooperation with other developing countries. China's South-South cooperation with Suriname has included a number of large-scale infrastructure projects, including port rehabilitation and road construction. Brazil signed agreements to cooperate with Suriname in education, health, agriculture, and energy production.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[50]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suriname&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Suriname" class="mw-redirect" title="Military of Suriname">Military of Suriname</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The Armed Forces of Suriname have three branches: the Army, the Air Force, and the Navy. The president of the Republic, <a href="/wiki/Chan_Santokhi" title="Chan Santokhi">Chan Santokhi</a>, is the Supreme Commander-in-Chief of the Armed Forces (<i>Opperbevelhebber van de Strijdkrachten</i>). The president is assisted by the minister of defence. Beneath the president and minister of defence is the commander of the armed forces (<i>Bevelhebber van de Strijdkrachten</i>). The military branches and regional military commands report to the commander. </p>
      <p>After the creation of the <a href="/wiki/Statute_of_the_Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands" class="mw-redirect" title="Statute of the Kingdom of the Netherlands">Statute of the Kingdom of the Netherlands</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Netherlands_Army" title="Royal Netherlands Army">Royal Netherlands Army</a> was entrusted with the defense of Suriname, while the defense of the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_Antilles" title="Netherlands Antilles">Netherlands Antilles</a> was the responsibility of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Netherlands_Navy" title="Royal Netherlands Navy">Royal Netherlands Navy</a>. The army set up a separate <i>Troepenmacht in Suriname</i> (Forces in Suriname, TRIS). Upon independence in 1975, this force was turned into the <i>Surinaamse Krijgsmacht</i> (SKM):, Surinamese Armed Forces. On 25 February 1980, a group of 15 non-commissioned officers and one junior SKM officer, under the leadership of Dési Bouterse, overthrew the government. Subsequently, the SKM was rebranded as <i>Nationaal Leger</i> (NL), National Army. </p>
      <p>In 1965, the Dutch and Americans used Suriname's Coronie site for multiple Nike Apache sounding rocket launches.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[51]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suriname&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Suriname_with_disputed_territories.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Suriname_with_disputed_territories.jpg/220px-Suriname_with_disputed_territories.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="265" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Suriname_with_disputed_territories.jpg/330px-Suriname_with_disputed_territories.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Suriname_with_disputed_territories.jpg/440px-Suriname_with_disputed_territories.jpg 2x" data-file-width="497" data-file-height="599"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Suriname_with_disputed_territories.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Map of Suriname
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Suriname" title="Districts of Suriname">Districts of Suriname</a> and <a href="/wiki/Resorts_of_Suriname" title="Resorts of Suriname">Resorts of Suriname</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The country is divided into ten administrative districts, each headed by a district commissioner appointed by the president, who also has the power of dismissal. Suriname is further subdivided into 62 resorts (ressorten). </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suriname&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Suriname" title="Geography of Suriname">Geography of Suriname</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:View_of_Brokopondo_Reservoir_(33537723975).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/View_of_Brokopondo_Reservoir_%2833537723975%29.jpg/220px-View_of_Brokopondo_Reservoir_%2833537723975%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/View_of_Brokopondo_Reservoir_%2833537723975%29.jpg/330px-View_of_Brokopondo_Reservoir_%2833537723975%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/View_of_Brokopondo_Reservoir_%2833537723975%29.jpg/440px-View_of_Brokopondo_Reservoir_%2833537723975%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4896" data-file-height="2752"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:View_of_Brokopondo_Reservoir_(33537723975).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Brokopondo_Reservoir" title="Brokopondo Reservoir">Brokopondo Reservoir</a> surrounded by tropical rainforest
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Morning_fog_(2719242329).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Morning_fog_%282719242329%29.jpg/220px-Morning_fog_%282719242329%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Morning_fog_%282719242329%29.jpg/330px-Morning_fog_%282719242329%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Morning_fog_%282719242329%29.jpg/440px-Morning_fog_%282719242329%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="819"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Morning_fog_(2719242329).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Coppename_River" title="Coppename River">Coppename river</a>, one of many rivers in the interior
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Leatherback_Turtle_near_Galibi.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Leatherback_Turtle_near_Galibi.jpg/220px-Leatherback_Turtle_near_Galibi.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Leatherback_Turtle_near_Galibi.jpg/330px-Leatherback_Turtle_near_Galibi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/Leatherback_Turtle_near_Galibi.jpg/440px-Leatherback_Turtle_near_Galibi.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Leatherback_Turtle_near_Galibi.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Leatherback_sea_turtle" title="Leatherback sea turtle">Leatherback sea turtle</a> on the beach near the village of Galibi
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Suriname is the smallest independent country in South America. Situated on the <a href="/wiki/Guiana_Shield" title="Guiana Shield">Guiana Shield</a>, it lies mostly between latitudes <a href="/wiki/1st_parallel_north" title="1st parallel north">1°</a> and <a href="/wiki/6th_parallel_north" title="6th parallel north">6°N</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/54th_meridian_west" title="54th meridian west">54°</a> and <a href="/wiki/58th_meridian_west" title="58th meridian west">58°W</a>. The country can be divided into two main geographic regions. The northern, lowland coastal area (roughly above the line Albina-Paranam-Wageningen) has been cultivated, and most of the population lives here. The southern part consists of tropical <a href="/wiki/Rainforest" title="Rainforest">rainforest</a> and sparsely inhabited <a href="/wiki/Savanna" title="Savanna">savanna</a> along the border with <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, covering about 80% of Suriname's land surface. </p>
      <p>The two main mountain ranges are the <a href="/wiki/Bakhuys_Mountains" class="mw-redirect" title="Bakhuys Mountains">Bakhuys Mountains</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Van_Asch_Van_Wijck_Mountains" title="Van Asch Van Wijck Mountains">Van Asch Van Wijck Mountains</a>. <a href="/wiki/Julianatop" title="Julianatop">Julianatop</a> is the highest mountain in the country at 1,286 metres (4,219&nbsp;ft) above sea level. Other mountains include <a href="/wiki/Tafelberg,_Suriname" title="Tafelberg, Suriname">Tafelberg</a> at 1,026 metres (3,366&nbsp;ft), Mount <a href="/wiki/Kasikasima" title="Kasikasima">Kasikasima</a> at 718 metres (2,356&nbsp;ft), Goliathberg at 358 metres (1,175&nbsp;ft) and <a href="/wiki/Voltzberg" title="Voltzberg">Voltzberg</a> at 240 metres (790&nbsp;ft). </p>
      <p>Suriname contains six terrestrial ecoregions: <a href="/wiki/Guayanan_Highlands_moist_forests" class="mw-redirect" title="Guayanan Highlands moist forests">Guayanan Highlands moist forests</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guianan_moist_forests" title="Guianan moist forests">Guianan moist forests</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paramaribo_swamp_forests" title="Paramaribo swamp forests">Paramaribo swamp forests</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tepuis" class="mw-redirect" title="Tepuis">Tepuis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guianan_savanna" title="Guianan savanna">Guianan savanna</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Guianan_mangroves" title="Guianan mangroves">Guianan mangroves</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-55">[53]</a></sup> Its forest cover is 90.2%, the highest of any nation in the world. The country had a 2019 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 9.39/10, ranking it 5th globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-56">[54]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Borders">Borders</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suriname&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Borders">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Borders_of_Suriname" title="Borders of Suriname">Borders of Suriname</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Suriname_location_map.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Suriname_location_map.svg/220px-Suriname_location_map.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="224" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Suriname_location_map.svg/330px-Suriname_location_map.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Suriname_location_map.svg/440px-Suriname_location_map.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1181" data-file-height="1205"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Suriname_location_map.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Disputed areas shown on the map of Suriname (left and right, gray areas)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Suriname is situated between <a href="/wiki/French_Guiana" title="French Guiana">French Guiana</a> to the east and <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a> to the west. The southern border is shared with <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> and the northern border is the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic</a> coast. The southernmost borders with French Guiana and Guyana are disputed by these countries along the <a href="/wiki/Maroni_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Maroni River">Marowijne</a> and <a href="/wiki/Courantyne_River" title="Courantyne River">Corantijn</a> rivers, respectively, while a part of the disputed <a href="/wiki/Maritime_boundary" title="Maritime boundary">maritime boundary</a> with Guyana was arbitrated by the <a href="/wiki/Permanent_Court_of_Arbitration" title="Permanent Court of Arbitration">Permanent Court of Arbitration</a> convened under the rules set out in <a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/United_Nations_Convention_on_the_Law_of_the_Sea/Annex_VII" class="extiw" title="s:United Nations Convention on the Law of the Sea/Annex VII">Annex VII</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Convention_on_the_Law_of_the_Sea" title="United Nations Convention on the Law of the Sea">United Nations Convention on the Law of the Sea</a> on 20 September 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[55]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[56]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suriname&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_SUR_present.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Koppen-Geiger_Map_SUR_present.svg/220px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_SUR_present.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="159" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Koppen-Geiger_Map_SUR_present.svg/330px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_SUR_present.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Koppen-Geiger_Map_SUR_present.svg/440px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_SUR_present.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1173" data-file-height="850"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_SUR_present.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Suriname map of Köppen climate classification
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Lying <a href="/wiki/2nd_parallel_north" title="2nd parallel north">2</a> to <a href="/wiki/5th_parallel_north" title="5th parallel north">5 degrees north</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Equator" title="Equator">equator</a>, Suriname has a very hot and wet <a href="/wiki/Tropical_climate" title="Tropical climate">tropical climate</a>, and temperatures do not vary much throughout the year. Average relative humidity is between 80% and 90%. Its average temperature ranges from 29 to 34 degrees Celsius (84 to 93 degrees Fahrenheit). Due to the high humidity, actual temperatures are distorted and may therefore feel up to 6 degrees Celsius (11 degrees Fahrenheit) hotter than the recorded temperature. The year has two <a href="/wiki/Wet_season" title="Wet season">wet seasons</a>, from April to August and from November to February. It also has two <a href="/wiki/Dry_season" title="Dry season">dry seasons</a>, from August to November and February to April. </p> 
      <div class="excerpt-block">
       <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r952607947">.mw-parser-output .excerpt .selflink{font-weight:normal}.mw-parser-output .excerpt-indicator{border-left:3px solid #c8ccd1;margin:1em 0;padding-left:1em}</style>
       <div class="dablink excerpt-hat">
        <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable dablink selfref">
         This section is an excerpt from <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_in_Suriname" title="Climate change in Suriname">Climate change in Suriname</a><i><span class="mw-editsection-like plainlinks"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Climate_change_in_Suriname&amp;action=edit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></i>
        </div>
       </div>
       <div class="excerpt"> <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_in_Suriname" title="Climate change in Suriname">Climate change in Suriname</a> is leading to warmer temperatures and more <a href="/wiki/Extreme_weather" title="Extreme weather">extreme weather</a> events in Suriname. As a relatively poor country, its contributions to global <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a> have been limited. Because of the large forest cover, the country has been running a <a href="/wiki/Carbon_dioxide_removal" title="Carbon dioxide removal">carbon negative</a> economy since 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-Climate_change_in_Suriname_:3_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Climate_change_in_Suriname_:3-59">[57]</a></sup>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nature_reserves">Nature reserves</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suriname&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Nature reserves">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Located in the upper <a href="/wiki/Coppename_River" title="Coppename River">Coppename River</a> <a href="/wiki/Drainage_basin" title="Drainage basin">watershed</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Central_Suriname_Nature_Reserve" title="Central Suriname Nature Reserve">Central Suriname Nature Reserve</a> has been designated a UNESCO <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a> for its unspoiled forests and <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">biodiversity</a>. There are many national parks in the country including Galibi National Reserve along the coast; <a href="/wiki/Brownsberg_Nature_Park" title="Brownsberg Nature Park">Brownsberg Nature Park</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eilerts_de_Haan_Nature_Park" class="mw-redirect" title="Eilerts de Haan Nature Park">Eilerts de Haan Nature Park</a> in central Suriname; and the <a href="/wiki/Sipaliwani_Nature_Reserve" class="mw-redirect" title="Sipaliwani Nature Reserve">Sipaliwani Nature Reserve</a> on the Brazilian border. In all, 16% of the country's land area is national parks and lakes, according to the UNEP World Conservation Monitoring Centre.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[58]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suriname&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Suriname" title="Economy of Suriname">Economy of Suriname</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Suriname_Export_Treemap.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Suriname_Export_Treemap.png/220px-Suriname_Export_Treemap.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Suriname_Export_Treemap.png/330px-Suriname_Export_Treemap.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Suriname_Export_Treemap.png/440px-Suriname_Export_Treemap.png 2x" data-file-width="959" data-file-height="751"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Suriname_Export_Treemap.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Suriname exports, 2012, including artificial <a href="/wiki/Corundum" title="Corundum">corundum</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Suriname's democracy gained some strength after the turbulent 1990s, and its economy became more diversified and less dependent on Dutch financial assistance. <a href="/wiki/Bauxite" title="Bauxite">Bauxite</a> (aluminium ore) mining used to be a strong revenue source. The discovery and exploitation of oil and gold has added substantially to Suriname's economic independence. Agriculture, especially rice and bananas, remains a strong component of the economy, and <a href="/wiki/Ecotourism" title="Ecotourism">ecotourism</a> is providing new economic opportunities. More than 93% of Suriname's land-mass consists of unspoiled rain forest; with the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/Central_Suriname_Nature_Reserve" title="Central Suriname Nature Reserve">Central Suriname Nature Reserve</a> in 1998, Suriname signalled its commitment to conservation of this precious resource. The Central Suriname Nature Reserve became a <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a> in 2000. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Financien.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Financien.JPG/220px-Financien.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="122" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Financien.JPG/330px-Financien.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Financien.JPG/440px-Financien.JPG 2x" data-file-width="702" data-file-height="389"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Financien.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Ministry of Finance
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The economy of Suriname was dominated by the bauxite industry, which accounted for more than 15% of GDP and 70% of export earnings up to 2016. Other main export products include rice, bananas, and <a href="/wiki/Shrimp" title="Shrimp">shrimp</a>. Suriname has recently started exploiting some of its sizeable <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">oil</a><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[59]</a></sup> and gold<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[60]</a></sup> reserves. About a quarter of the people work in the agricultural sector. The Surinamese economy is very dependent on commerce, its main trade partners being the Netherlands, the United States, Canada, and <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> countries, mainly <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</a> and the islands of the former <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_Antilles" title="Netherlands Antilles">Netherlands Antilles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[61]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>After assuming power in the fall of 1996, the <a href="/wiki/Jules_Wijdenbosch" title="Jules Wijdenbosch">Wijdenbosch</a> government ended the <a href="/wiki/Structural_adjustment" title="Structural adjustment">structural adjustment</a> program of the previous government, claiming it was unfair to the poorer elements of society. Tax revenues fell as old taxes lapsed and the government failed to implement new tax alternatives. By the end of 1997, the allocation of new Dutch development funds was frozen as Surinamese Government relations with the Netherlands deteriorated. Economic growth slowed in 1998, with decline in the mining, construction, and <a href="/wiki/Utility" title="Utility">utility</a> sectors. Rampant government expenditures, poor tax collection, a bloated civil service, and reduced foreign aid in 1999 contributed to the fiscal deficit, estimated at 11% of GDP. The government sought to cover this deficit through monetary expansion, which led to a dramatic increase in inflation. It takes longer on average to register a new business in Suriname than virtually any other country in the world (694 days or about 99 weeks).<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[62]</a></sup> </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>GDP (2010 est.): U.S. $4.794 billion.</li> 
       <li>Annual growth rate real GDP (2010 est.): 3.5%.</li> 
       <li>Per capita GDP (2010 est.): U.S. $9,900.</li> 
       <li>Inflation (2007): 6.4%.</li> 
       <li>Natural resources: Bauxite, gold, oil, iron ore, other minerals; forests; hydroelectric potential; fish and shrimp.</li> 
       <li>Agriculture: Products—rice, bananas, timber, palm kernels, coconuts, peanuts, citrus fruits, and forest products.</li> 
       <li>Industry: Types—alumina, oil, gold, fish, shrimp, lumber.</li> 
       <li>Trade: 
        <ul>
         <li>Exports (2012): $2.563 billion: alumina, gold, crude oil, lumber, shrimp and fish, rice, bananas. Major consumers: US 26.1%, Belgium 17.6%, UAE 12.1%, Canada 10.4%, Guyana 6.5%, France 5.6%, Barbados 4.7%.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_16-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-16">[14]</a></sup></li> 
         <li>Imports (2012): $1.782 billion: capital equipment, petroleum, foodstuffs, cotton, consumer goods. Major suppliers: US 25.8%, Netherlands 15.8%, China 9.8%, UAE 7.9%, Antigua and Barbuda 7.3%, Netherlands Antilles 5.4%, Japan 4.2%.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_16-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-16">[14]</a></sup></li>
        </ul></li>
      </ul> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suriname&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Suriname" title="Demographics of Suriname">Demographics of Suriname</a> and <a href="/wiki/Surinamese_people" title="Surinamese people">Surinamese people</a>
      </div>

      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Suriname_demography.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Suriname_demography.png/220px-Suriname_demography.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="129" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Suriname_demography.png/330px-Suriname_demography.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Suriname_demography.png/440px-Suriname_demography.png 2x" data-file-width="724" data-file-height="426"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Suriname_demography.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The population of Suriname from 1961 to 2003, in units of 1000. The slowdown and decline in population growth ~1969–1985 reflects a mass migration to the Netherlands and French Guiana.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>According to the 2012 census, Suriname had a population of 541,638 inhabitants.<sup id="cite_ref-statistics-suriname1_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statistics-suriname1-5">[5]</a></sup> The Surinamese populace is characterized by its high level of diversity, wherein no particular demographic group constitutes a majority. This is a legacy of centuries of Dutch rule, which entailed successive periods of forced, contracted, or voluntary migration by various nationalities and ethnic groups from around the world. </p> 
      <div class="barbox tleft" style="overflow-x: auto;"> 
       <div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;">
