       </div> 
      </div> 
      <p>The largest ethnic group are the <a href="/wiki/Indo-Surinamese" title="Indo-Surinamese">East Indians</a> which form about 27.4% of the population. They are descendants of 19th-century indentured workers from <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, hailing mostly from the modern Indian states of <a href="/wiki/Bihar" title="Bihar">Bihar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jharkhand" title="Jharkhand">Jharkhand</a>, and Eastern <a href="/wiki/Uttar_Pradesh" title="Uttar Pradesh">Uttar Pradesh</a> along the Nepali border. The largest group of people are however the <a href="/wiki/Afro-Surinamese" class="mw-redirect" title="Afro-Surinamese">Afro-Surinamese</a>; around 37.4%. They are usually divided into two cultural/ethnic groups: the <a href="/wiki/Creole_peoples" title="Creole peoples">Creoles</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Maroon_(people)" class="mw-redirect" title="Maroon (people)">Maroons</a>. Surinamese <a href="/wiki/Maroon_(people)" class="mw-redirect" title="Maroon (people)">Maroons</a>, whose ancestors are mostly runaway slaves that fled to the interior, comprise 21.7% of the population; they are divided into six tribes: <a href="/wiki/Ndyuka_people" title="Ndyuka people">Ndyuka</a> (Aucans), <a href="/wiki/Saramaka" title="Saramaka">Saramaccans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paramaccan" class="mw-redirect" title="Paramaccan">Paramaccans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kwinti" class="mw-redirect" title="Kwinti">Kwinti</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aluku" title="Aluku">Aluku</a> (Boni) and <a href="/wiki/Matawai_people" title="Matawai people">Matawai</a>. Surinamese <a href="/wiki/Creole_peoples" title="Creole peoples">Creoles</a>, mixed people descending from African slaves and Europeans (mostly Dutch), form 15.7% of the population. <a href="/wiki/Javanese_Surinamese" title="Javanese Surinamese">Javanese</a> make up 14% of the population, and like the East Indians, descend largely from workers contracted from the island of <a href="/wiki/Java" title="Java">Java</a> in the former <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_Indies" title="Dutch East Indies">Dutch East Indies</a> (modern <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-javanese_in_suriname_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-javanese_in_suriname-66">[64]</a></sup> 13.4% of the population identifies as being of mixed ethnic heritage. <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Surinamese" title="Chinese Surinamese">Chinese</a>, originating from 19th-century indentured workers and some recent migration, make up 7.3% of the population. Other groups include <a href="/wiki/Lebanese_people" title="Lebanese people">Lebanese</a>, primarily <a href="/wiki/Maronites" title="Maronites">Maronites</a>; <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Suriname" title="History of the Jews in Suriname">Jews</a> of <a href="/wiki/Sephardi_Jews" title="Sephardi Jews">Sephardic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ashkenazi_Jews" title="Ashkenazi Jews">Ashkenazi</a> origin, whose center of population was the community of <a href="/wiki/Jodensavanne" title="Jodensavanne">Jodensavanne</a>. Various <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">indigenous peoples</a> make up 3.7% of the population, with the main groups being the <a href="/wiki/Akurio_people" title="Akurio people">Akurio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arawak" title="Arawak">Arawak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kalina_people" title="Kalina people">Kalina</a> (Caribs), <a href="/wiki/Tiriy%C3%B3_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Tiriyó people">Tiriyó</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wayana_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Wayana people">Wayana</a>. They live mainly in the districts of <a href="/wiki/Paramaribo" title="Paramaribo">Paramaribo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wanica_District" title="Wanica District">Wanica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Para_District" title="Para District">Para</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marowijne_District" title="Marowijne District">Marowijne</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sipaliwini_District" title="Sipaliwini District">Sipaliwini</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> A small but influential number of <a href="/wiki/White_Surinamese" title="White Surinamese">Europeans</a> remain in the country, comprising about 1% of the population. They are descended mostly from <a href="/wiki/Dutch_people" title="Dutch people">Dutch</a> 19th-century immigrant farmers, known as "<a href="/wiki/Dutch_Surinamese" title="Dutch Surinamese">Boeroes</a>" (derived from <i>boer</i>, the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a> word for "farmer"), and to a lesser degree other European groups, such as <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_people" title="Portuguese people">Portuguese</a>. Many Boeroes <a href="/wiki/White_flight" title="White flight">left after independence in 1975</a>. </p>
      <p>More recently Suriname has seen a new wave of immigrants; many of them have no legal status. These are namely <a href="/wiki/Brazilians_in_Suriname" title="Brazilians in Suriname">Brazilians</a> (many of them laborers mining for gold), <a href="/wiki/Cubans" title="Cubans">Cubans</a>, <a href="/wiki/People_of_the_Dominican_Republic" title="People of the Dominican Republic">Dominicans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Haitians" title="Haitians">Haitians</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[65]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The vast majority of Suriname's inhabitants (about 90%) live in <a href="/wiki/Paramaribo" title="Paramaribo">Paramaribo</a> or on the coast. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Emigration">Emigration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suriname&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Emigration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tropenmuseum_Royal_Tropical_Institute_Objectnumber_60008924_Een_groep_Brits-Indische_immigranten.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Tropenmuseum_Royal_Tropical_Institute_Objectnumber_60008924_Een_groep_Brits-Indische_immigranten.jpg/220px-Tropenmuseum_Royal_Tropical_Institute_Objectnumber_60008924_Een_groep_Brits-Indische_immigranten.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Tropenmuseum_Royal_Tropical_Institute_Objectnumber_60008924_Een_groep_Brits-Indische_immigranten.jpg/330px-Tropenmuseum_Royal_Tropical_Institute_Objectnumber_60008924_Een_groep_Brits-Indische_immigranten.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Tropenmuseum_Royal_Tropical_Institute_Objectnumber_60008924_Een_groep_Brits-Indische_immigranten.jpg/440px-Tropenmuseum_Royal_Tropical_Institute_Objectnumber_60008924_Een_groep_Brits-Indische_immigranten.jpg 2x" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="548"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tropenmuseum_Royal_Tropical_Institute_Objectnumber_60008924_Een_groep_Brits-Indische_immigranten.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Immigrants from <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The choice of becoming Surinamese or Dutch citizens in the years leading up to Suriname's independence in 1975 led to a mass migration to the Netherlands. This migration continued in the period immediately after independence and during military rule in the 1980s and for largely economic reasons extended throughout the 1990s. The <a href="/wiki/Surinamese_people_in_the_Netherlands" title="Surinamese people in the Netherlands">Surinamese community</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a> numbered 350,300 as of 2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Suriname&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> (including children and grandchildren of Suriname migrants born in The Netherlands); this is compared to approximately 566,000<sup id="cite_ref-cia_16-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-16">[14]</a></sup> Surinamese in Suriname itself. </p>
      <p>According to the <a href="/wiki/International_Organization_for_Migration" title="International Organization for Migration">International Organization for Migration</a>, around 272,600 people from Suriname lived in other countries in the late 2010s, in particular in the Netherlands (ca 192,000), the <a href="/wiki/French_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="French Republic">French Republic</a> (ca 25,000, most of them in <a href="/wiki/French_Guiana" title="French Guiana">French Guiana</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[note 3]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> (ca 15,000), <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a> (ca 5,000), <a href="/wiki/Aruba" title="Aruba">Aruba</a> (ca 1,500), and <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> (ca 1,000).<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[66]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suriname&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Suriname" title="Religion in Suriname">Religion in Suriname</a>
      </div>

      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:MoscheeSynagoge.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/MoscheeSynagoge.jpg/220px-MoscheeSynagoge.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/MoscheeSynagoge.jpg/330px-MoscheeSynagoge.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/MoscheeSynagoge.jpg/440px-MoscheeSynagoge.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:MoscheeSynagoge.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Synagogue and mosque adjacent to each other in Paramaribo
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Suriname's religious makeup is heterogeneous and reflective of the country's multicultural character. According to PEW research from 2012, the country comprises Christians (51.6), Buddhists (&lt;1%), folk (5.3%), Hindu (19.8%), Jew, (&lt;1%), Muslim (15.2%), other (1.8%), unaffiliated (5.4%).<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[67]</a></sup> According to the 2012 census, 48.4% were Christians;<sup id="cite_ref-CENSUS2012_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CENSUS2012-7">[7]</a></sup> 26.7% of Surinamese were <a href="/wiki/Protestants" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestants">Protestants</a> (11.18% <a href="/wiki/Pentecostal" class="mw-redirect" title="Pentecostal">Pentecostal</a>, 11.16% <a href="/wiki/Moravian_Church" title="Moravian Church">Moravian</a>, and 4.4% of various other Protestant denominations) and 21.6% were <a href="/wiki/Catholics" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholics">Catholics</a>. <a href="/wiki/Hindu" class="mw-redirect" title="Hindu">Hindus</a> formed the second-largest religious group in Suriname, comprising 22.3% of the population,<sup id="cite_ref-CENSUS2012_7-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CENSUS2012-7">[7]</a></sup> the third largest proportion of any country in the Western Hemisphere after <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</a>, both of which also have large proportions of <a href="/wiki/Indo-Caribbeans" title="Indo-Caribbeans">Indians</a>. Almost all practitioners of <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a> are found among the Indo-Surinamese population. <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslims</a> constitute 13.9% of the population, the highest proportion of Muslims in the Americas; they are largely of Javanese or Indian descent.<sup id="cite_ref-CENSUS2012_7-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CENSUS2012-7">[7]</a></sup> Other religious groups include <a href="/wiki/Winti" title="Winti">Winti</a> (1.8%),<sup id="cite_ref-CENSUS2012_7-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CENSUS2012-7">[7]</a></sup> an <a href="/wiki/Afro-American_religion" class="mw-redirect" title="Afro-American religion">Afro-American religion</a> practiced mostly by those of Maroon ancestry; <a href="/wiki/Kejaw%C3%A8n" title="Kejawèn">Javanism</a> (0.8%),<sup id="cite_ref-CENSUS2012_7-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CENSUS2012-7">[7]</a></sup> a syncretic faith found among some Javanese Surinamese; and various indigenous folk traditions that are often incorporated into one of the larger religions (usually Christianity). In the 2012 census, 7.5% of the population declared they had "no religion", while a further 3.2% left the question unanswered.<sup id="cite_ref-CENSUS2012_7-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CENSUS2012-7">[7]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suriname&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Butcher_Paramaribo_market.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Butcher_Paramaribo_market.jpg/170px-Butcher_Paramaribo_market.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Butcher_Paramaribo_market.jpg/255px-Butcher_Paramaribo_market.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Butcher_Paramaribo_market.jpg/340px-Butcher_Paramaribo_market.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2112" data-file-height="2816"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Butcher_Paramaribo_market.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Butcher in the <a href="/wiki/Central_Market_(Paramaribo)" title="Central Market (Paramaribo)">Central Market</a> in Paramaribo with signs written in <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Suriname has a total of around 14 local languages, but <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a> is the sole official language and is the language used in education, government, business, and the media.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_16-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-16">[14]</a></sup> Over 60% of the population are <a href="/wiki/First_language" title="First language">native speakers</a> of Dutch<sup id="cite_ref-taalgebied_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-taalgebied-71">[68]</a></sup> and around 20%-30% speak it as a second language. In 2004, Suriname became an associate member of the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Language_Union" title="Dutch Language Union">Dutch Language Union</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[69]</a></sup> It is the only Dutch-speaking country in South America and the only independent nation in the Americas in which Dutch is spoken by a majority of the population and one of the two non-<a href="/wiki/Romance_languages" title="Romance languages">Romance</a>-speaking countries in South America, the other being English-speaking <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a>. </p>
      <p>In Paramaribo, Dutch is the main home language in two thirds of the households.<sup id="cite_ref-Census_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census-4">[4]</a></sup> The recognition of <i>"Surinaams-Nederlands"</i> ("<a href="/wiki/Surinamese_Dutch" title="Surinamese Dutch">Surinamese Dutch</a>") as a national dialect equal to <i>"Nederlands-Nederlands"</i> ("Dutch Dutch") and <i>"Vlaams-Nederlands"</i> ("Flemish Dutch") was expressed in 2009 by the publication of the <i>Woordenboek Surinaams Nederlands</i> (<i>Surinamese–Dutch Dictionary</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[70]</a></sup> It is the most commonly spoken language in urban areas; only in the interior of Suriname (namely parts of <a href="/wiki/Sipaliwini_District" title="Sipaliwini District">Sipaliwini</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brokopondo_District" title="Brokopondo District">Brokopondo</a>) is Dutch seldom spoken. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Sranan_Tongo" title="Sranan Tongo">Sranan Tongo</a>, a local English-based <a href="/wiki/Creole_language" title="Creole language">creole language</a>, is the most widely used <a href="/wiki/Vernacular_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Vernacular language">vernacular language</a> in daily life and business. Together with Dutch, it is considered to be the one of the two principal languages of Surinamese <a href="/wiki/Diglossia" title="Diglossia">diglossia</a>. Both are further influenced by other spoken languages which are spoken primarily within ethnic communities. Sranan Tongo is often used interchangeably with Dutch depending on the formality of the setting; Dutch is seen as a <a href="/wiki/Prestige_dialect" class="mw-redirect" title="Prestige dialect">prestige dialect</a> and Sranan Tongo the common <a href="/wiki/Vernacular" title="Vernacular">vernacular</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT2008_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT2008-74">[71]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Hindustani" title="Caribbean Hindustani">Caribbean Hindustani</a> or Sarnami, a dialect of <a href="/wiki/Bhojpuri_language" title="Bhojpuri language">Bhojpuri</a>, is the third-most used language. It is primarily spoken by the descendants of East Indian indentured labourers from the former <a href="/wiki/British_Raj" title="British Raj">British India</a>. </p>
      <p>The six <a href="/wiki/Maroon_(people)" class="mw-redirect" title="Maroon (people)">Maroon</a> languages of Suriname are also considered English-based creole languages, and include <a href="/wiki/Saramaccan_language" title="Saramaccan language">Saramaccan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ndyuka_(language)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ndyuka (language)">Aukan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aluku" title="Aluku">Aluku</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paramakans" class="mw-redirect" title="Paramakans">Paramaccan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Matawai_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Matawai language">Matawai</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kwinti_language" title="Kwinti language">Kwinti</a>. </p>
      <p>Aluku, Paramaccan and Kwinti are so mutually intelligible with Aukan, that they can be consindered dialects of the Aukan language. The same can be said about Matawai, which is mutually intelligible with Saramaka. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Javanese_language" title="Javanese language">Javanese</a> is used by the descendants of Javanese indentured labourers. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">Amerindian</a> languages, include <a href="/wiki/Carib_languages" class="mw-redirect" title="Carib languages">Carib</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arawakan_languages" title="Arawakan languages">Arawak</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tiriy%C3%B3_language" title="Tiriyó language">Tiriyó</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wayana_language" title="Wayana language">Wayana</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Hakka_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Hakka language">Hakka</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cantonese_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Cantonese language">Cantonese</a> are spoken by the descendants of the Chinese indentured labourers. <a href="/wiki/Standard_Mandarin" class="mw-redirect" title="Standard Mandarin">Mandarin</a> is spoken by the recent wave of Chinese immigrants. </p>
      <p>Other languages not really local to Suriname, but also used include: <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> and <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Largest_cities">Largest cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suriname&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Largest cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The national capital, Paramaribo, is by far the dominant urban area, accounting for nearly half of Suriname's population and most of its urban residents; indeed, its population is greater than the next nine largest cities combined. Most municipalities are located within the capital's metropolitan area, or along the densely populated coastline. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suriname&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Suriname" title="Culture of Suriname">Culture of Suriname</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_Suriname" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism in Suriname">Roman Catholicism in Suriname</a>, <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Suriname" title="Music of Suriname">Music of Suriname</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hinduism_in_South_America" title="Hinduism in South America">Hinduism in South America</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Owing to the country's multicultural heritage, Suriname celebrates a variety of distinct ethnic and religious festivals. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="National_holidays">National holidays</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suriname&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: National holidays">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <ul>
       <li>1 January – New Year's Day</li> 
       <li>6 January – <a href="/wiki/Three_Kings_Day" class="mw-redirect" title="Three Kings Day">Three Kings Day</a></li> 
       <li>January – <a href="/wiki/World_Religion_Day" title="World Religion Day">World Religion Day</a></li> 
       <li>January/February – <a href="/wiki/Chinese_New_Year" title="Chinese New Year">Chinese New Year</a></li> 
       <li>March (varies) – <a href="/wiki/Holi" title="Holi">Holi</a></li> 
       <li>March/April – <a href="/wiki/Good_Friday" title="Good Friday">Good Friday</a></li> 
       <li>March/April – Easter</li> 
       <li>1 May – Labour Day</li> 
       <li>May/June – <a href="/wiki/Ascension_day" class="mw-redirect" title="Ascension day">Ascension day</a></li> 
       <li>5 June – <a href="/wiki/Indian_Arrival_Day" title="Indian Arrival Day">Indian Arrival Day</a></li> 
       <li>1 July – <a href="/wiki/Keti_Koti" class="mw-redirect" title="Keti Koti">Keti Koti</a> (Emancipation Day – end of slavery)</li> 
       <li>8 August – <a href="/wiki/Javanese_Surinamese" title="Javanese Surinamese">Javanese Arrival Day</a></li> 
       <li>9 August – <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_People%27s_Day" class="mw-redirect" title="Indigenous People's Day">Indigenous People's Day</a></li> 
       <li>10 October – Day of the Maroons</li> 
       <li>20 October – <a href="/wiki/Chinese_Surinamese" title="Chinese Surinamese">Chinese Arrival day</a></li> 
       <li>October/November – <a href="/wiki/Diwali" title="Diwali">Diwali</a></li> 
       <li>25 November – <a href="/wiki/Independence_Day" class="mw-redirect" title="Independence Day">Independence Day</a></li> 
       <li>25 December – Christmas</li> 
       <li>26 December – <a href="/wiki/Boxing_Day" title="Boxing Day">Boxing Day</a></li> 
       <li>varies - <a href="/wiki/Eid-ul-adha" class="mw-redirect" title="Eid-ul-adha">Eid-ul-adha</a></li>
      </ul> 
      <p>There are several Hindu and Islamic national holidays like Diwali (<a href="/wiki/Deepavali" class="mw-redirect" title="Deepavali">deepavali</a>), <a href="/wiki/Phagwa" class="mw-redirect" title="Phagwa">Phagwa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eid_ul-Fitr" class="mw-redirect" title="Eid ul-Fitr">Eid ul-Fitr</a> and Eid-ul-adha. These holidays do not have fixed dates on the <a href="/wiki/Gregorian_calendar" title="Gregorian calendar">Gregorian calendar</a>, as they are based on the <a href="/wiki/Hindu_calendar" title="Hindu calendar">Hindu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Islamic_calendar" title="Islamic calendar">Islamic calendars</a>, respectively. As of 2020, Eid-ul-adha is a national holiday, and equal to a Sunday.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[73]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There are several holidays which are unique to Suriname. These include the Indian, Javanese and Chinese arrival days. They celebrate the arrival of the first ships with their respective immigrants. </p> 
      <h4><span id="New_Year.27s_Eve"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="New_Year's_Eve">New Year's Eve</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suriname&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: New Year's Eve">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Kerstoudjaar_037.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Kerstoudjaar_037.jpg/220px-Kerstoudjaar_037.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Kerstoudjaar_037.jpg/330px-Kerstoudjaar_037.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Kerstoudjaar_037.jpg/440px-Kerstoudjaar_037.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Kerstoudjaar_037.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Pagara (red firecracker ribbons)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>New Year's Eve in Suriname is called <i>Oud jaar</i>, <i>Owru Yari</i>, or "old year". It is during this period that the Surinamese population goes to the city's commercial district to watch "demonstrational <a href="/wiki/Fireworks" title="Fireworks">fireworks</a>". The bigger stores invest in these <a href="/wiki/Firecrackers" class="mw-redirect" title="Firecrackers">firecrackers</a> and display them out in the streets. Every year the length of them is compared, and high praises are given for the company that has imported the largest ribbon. </p>
      <p>These celebrations start at 10 in the morning and finish the next day. The day is usually filled with laughter, dance, music, and drinking. When the night starts, the big street parties are already at full capacity. The most popular fiesta is the one that is held at <a href="/w/index.php?title=Caf%C3%A9_%27t_Vat&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Café 't Vat (page does not exist)">café 't Vat</a> in the main tourist district. The parties there stop between 10 and 11 at night, after which people go home to light their pagaras (red-firecracker-ribbons) at midnight. After 12, the parties continue and the streets fill again until daybreak.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[74]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suriname&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The major sports in Suriname are <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">volleyball</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Suriname_Olympic_Committee" title="Suriname Olympic Committee">Suriname Olympic Committee</a> is the national governing body for sports in Suriname. The major <a href="/wiki/Mind_sport" title="Mind sport">mind sports</a> are <a href="/wiki/Chess" title="Chess">chess</a>, <a href="/wiki/Draughts" title="Draughts">draughts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bridge_(card_game)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bridge (card game)">bridge</a> and <a href="/wiki/Troefcall" title="Troefcall">troefcall</a>. </p>
      <p>Many Suriname-born football players and Dutch-born football players of Surinamese descent, like <a href="/wiki/Gerald_Vanenburg" title="Gerald Vanenburg">Gerald Vanenburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ruud_Gullit" title="Ruud Gullit">Ruud Gullit</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frank_Rijkaard" title="Frank Rijkaard">Frank Rijkaard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edgar_Davids" title="Edgar Davids">Edgar Davids</a>, <a href="/wiki/Clarence_Seedorf" title="Clarence Seedorf">Clarence Seedorf</a>, <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Kluivert" title="Patrick Kluivert">Patrick Kluivert</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aron_Winter" title="Aron Winter">Aron Winter</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georginio_Wijnaldum" title="Georginio Wijnaldum">Georginio Wijnaldum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Virgil_van_Dijk" title="Virgil van Dijk">Virgil van Dijk</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Floyd_Hasselbaink" title="Jimmy Floyd Hasselbaink">Jimmy Floyd Hasselbaink</a> have turned out to play for the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_national_football_team" title="Netherlands national football team">Dutch national team</a>. In 1999, <a href="/wiki/Humphrey_Mijnals" title="Humphrey Mijnals">Humphrey Mijnals</a>, who played for both <a href="/wiki/Suriname_national_football_team" title="Suriname national football team">Suriname</a> and the Netherlands, was elected Surinamese footballer of the century.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[75]</a></sup> Another famous player is <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9_Kamperveen" title="André Kamperveen">André Kamperveen</a>, who captained Suriname in the 1940s and was the first Surinamese to play professionally in the Netherlands. </p>
      <p>The most famous international track &amp; field athlete from Suriname is <a href="/wiki/Letitia_Vriesde" title="Letitia Vriesde">Letitia Vriesde</a>, who won a silver medal at the <a href="/wiki/1995_World_Championships_in_Athletics" title="1995 World Championships in Athletics">1995 World Championships</a> behind Ana Quirot in the 800 metres, the first medal won by a South American female athlete in World Championship competition. In addition, she also won a bronze medal at the <a href="/wiki/2001_World_Championships_in_Athletics" title="2001 World Championships in Athletics">2001 World Championships</a> and won several medals in the 800 and 1500 metres at the <a href="/wiki/Pan-American_Games" class="mw-redirect" title="Pan-American Games">Pan-American Games</a> and <a href="/wiki/Central_American_and_Caribbean_Games" title="Central American and Caribbean Games">Central American and Caribbean Games</a>. <a href="/wiki/Tommy_Asinga" title="Tommy Asinga">Tommy Asinga</a> also received acclaim for winning a bronze medal in the 800 metres at the <a href="/wiki/1991_Pan_American_Games" title="1991 Pan American Games">1991 Pan American Games</a>. </p>
      <p>Swimmer <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Nesty" title="Anthony Nesty">Anthony Nesty</a> is the only Olympic medalist for Suriname. He won gold in the 100-meter butterfly at the <a href="/wiki/1988_Summer_Olympics" title="1988 Summer Olympics">1988 Summer Olympics</a> in <a href="/wiki/Seoul" title="Seoul">Seoul</a> and he won bronze in the same discipline at the 1992 Summer Olympics in <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a>. Originally from <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</a>, he now lives in <a href="/wiki/Gainesville,_Florida" title="Gainesville, Florida">Gainesville, Florida</a>, and is the coach of the University of Florida, mainly coaching distance swimmers. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">Cricket</a> is popular in Suriname to some extent, influenced by its popularity <a href="/wiki/Cricket_in_the_Netherlands" title="Cricket in the Netherlands">in the Netherlands</a> and in neighbouring Guyana. The <a href="/wiki/Surinaamse_Cricket_Bond" class="mw-redirect" title="Surinaamse Cricket Bond">Surinaamse Cricket Bond</a> is an <a href="/wiki/List_of_International_Cricket_Council_members" title="List of International Cricket Council members">associate member</a> of the <a href="/wiki/International_Cricket_Council" title="International Cricket Council">International Cricket Council</a> (ICC). Suriname and Argentina were the only ICC associate members in South America when ICC had a three tiered membership, although Guyana is represented on the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies_Cricket_Board" class="mw-redirect" title="West Indies Cricket Board">West Indies Cricket Board</a>, a full member. <a href="/wiki/Suriname_national_cricket_team" title="Suriname national cricket team">The national cricket team</a> was ranked 47th in the world and sixth in the <a href="/wiki/ICC_Americas" title="ICC Americas">ICC Americas</a> region as of June 2014, and competes in the <a href="/wiki/World_Cricket_League" title="World Cricket League">World Cricket League</a> (WCL) and <a href="/wiki/ICC_Americas_Championship" title="ICC Americas Championship">ICC Americas Championship</a>. <a href="/wiki/Iris_Jharap" title="Iris Jharap">Iris Jharap</a>, born in Paramaribo, played <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_One_Day_International" title="Women's One Day International">women's One Day International</a> matches for <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_national_women%27s_cricket_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Netherlands national women's cricket team">the Dutch national side</a>, the only Surinamese to do so.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[76]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the sport of badminton the local heroes are <a href="/wiki/Virgil_Soeroredjo" title="Virgil Soeroredjo">Virgil Soeroredjo</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/Mitchel_Wongsodikromo" title="Mitchel Wongsodikromo">Mitchel Wongsodikromo</a> and also <a href="/wiki/Crystal_Leefmans" title="Crystal Leefmans">Crystal Leefmans</a>. All winning medals for Suriname at the <a href="/wiki/Carebaco_International" title="Carebaco International">Carebaco Caribbean Championships</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Central_American_and_Caribbean_Games" title="Central American and Caribbean Games">Central American and Caribbean Games</a> (CACSO Games)<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[77]</a></sup> and also at the <a href="/wiki/South_American_Games" title="South American Games">South American Games</a>, better known as the <a href="/wiki/ODESUR" title="ODESUR">ODESUR</a> Games. Virgil Soeroredjo also participated for Suriname at the <a href="/wiki/Badminton_at_the_2012_Summer_Olympics" title="Badminton at the 2012 Summer Olympics">2012 London Summer Olympics</a>, only the second badminton player, after <a href="/wiki/Oscar_Brandon" title="Oscar Brandon">Oscar Brandon</a>, for Suriname to achieve this.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[78]</a></sup> Current <a href="/wiki/Surinamese_National_Badminton_Championships" title="Surinamese National Badminton Championships">National Champion</a> <a href="/wiki/S%C3%B6ren_Opti" title="Sören Opti">Sören Opti</a> was the third Surinamese badminton player to participate at the <a href="/wiki/2016_Summer_Olympics" title="2016 Summer Olympics">Summer Olympics</a> in 2016. </p>
      <p>Multiple time <a href="/wiki/K-1" title="K-1">K-1</a> <a href="/wiki/Kickboxing" title="Kickboxing">kickboxing</a> world champions <a href="/wiki/Ernesto_Hoost" title="Ernesto Hoost">Ernesto Hoost</a> and <a href="/wiki/Remy_Bonjasky" title="Remy Bonjasky">Remy Bonjasky</a> were born in Suriname or are of Surinamese descent. Other kickboxing world champions include <a href="/wiki/Rayen_Simson" title="Rayen Simson">Rayen Simson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Melvin_Manhoef" title="Melvin Manhoef">Melvin Manhoef</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tyrone_Spong" title="Tyrone Spong">Tyrone Spong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jairzinho_Rozenstruik" title="Jairzinho Rozenstruik">Jairzinho Rozenstruik</a> and <a href="/wiki/Regian_Eersel" title="Regian Eersel">Regian Eersel</a>. </p>
      <p>Suriname also has a <a href="/wiki/Suriname_national_korfball_team" title="Suriname national korfball team">national korfball team</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Korfball" title="Korfball">korfball</a> being a Dutch sport. <a href="/wiki/Vinkensport" title="Vinkensport">Vinkensport</a> is also practised. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suriname&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Suriname" title="Transport in Suriname">Transport in Suriname</a>, <a href="/wiki/Desir%C3%A9_Delano_Bouterse_Highway" title="Desiré Delano Bouterse Highway">Desiré Delano Bouterse Highway</a>, and <a href="/wiki/East-West_Link_(Suriname)" title="East-West Link (Suriname)">East-West Link (Suriname)</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Suriname, along with neighboring <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a>, is one of only two countries on the mainland South American continent that drive on the left, although many vehicles are left hand drive as well as right hand drive.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[79]</a></sup> One explanation for this practice is that at the time of its colonization of Suriname, the Netherlands itself used left-hand traffic, also introducing the practice in the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_Indies" title="Dutch East Indies">Dutch East Indies</a>, now <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-New_Scientist_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-New_Scientist-83">[80]</a></sup> Another is that Suriname was first colonized by the British, and for practical reasons, this was not changed when it came under Dutch administration.<sup id="cite_ref-Kincaid_Rule_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kincaid_Rule-84">[81]</a></sup> Although the Netherlands converted to driving to the right at the end of the 18th century,<sup id="cite_ref-New_Scientist_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-New_Scientist-83">[80]</a></sup> Suriname did not. Road's length (2003): 4303&nbsp;km (of which 1119&nbsp;km are paved).<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[82]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air">Air</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suriname&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Air">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The country has 55 airports<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[83]</a></sup> (of which 6 are paved). The international airport is: <a href="/wiki/Johan_Adolf_Pengel_International_Airport" title="Johan Adolf Pengel International Airport">Johan Adolf Pengel International Airport</a>. </p>
      <p>Airlines with departures from Suriname: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Blue_Wing_Airlines" title="Blue Wing Airlines">Blue Wing Airlines</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Gum_Air" title="Gum Air">Gum Air</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Fly_All_Ways" title="Fly All Ways">Fly All Ways</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Surinam_Airways" title="Surinam Airways">Surinam Airways</a> <i>(SLM)</i></li>
      </ul> 
      <p>Airlines with arrivals in Suriname: </p> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Airlines" title="Caribbean Airlines">Caribbean Airlines</a> (Trinidad &amp; Tobago)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Insel_Air" title="Insel Air">Insel Air</a> (Curaçao)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/KLM" title="KLM">KLM</a> (Netherlands)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Gol_Transportes_A%C3%A9reos" class="mw-redirect" title="Gol Transportes Aéreos">Gol Transportes Aéreos</a> (Brazil)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Copa_Airlines" title="Copa Airlines">Copa Airlines</a> (Panama)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/TUI_Group#Airlines" title="TUI Group">Tui</a> (Netherlands)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Fly_All_Ways" title="Fly All Ways">Fly All Ways</a> (Curaçao), Cuba <i>(<a href="/wiki/Havana" title="Havana">Havana</a>)</i>, <i>(<a href="/wiki/Santiago_de_Cuba" title="Santiago de Cuba">Santiago de Cuba</a>)</i></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Surinam_Airways" title="Surinam Airways">Surinam Airways</a> <i>(SLM)</i> (<a href="/wiki/Aruba" title="Aruba">Aruba</a>), Brazil <i>(<a href="/wiki/Bel%C3%A9m" title="Belém">Belém</a>)</i>, (<a href="/wiki/Cura%C3%A7ao" title="Curaçao">Curaçao</a>), Guyana <i>(<a href="/wiki/Georgetown,_Guyana" title="Georgetown, Guyana">Georgetown</a>)</i>, Netherlands <i>(<a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a>)</i>, Trinidad &amp; Tobago <i>(<a href="/wiki/Port_of_Spain" title="Port of Spain">Port of Spain</a>)</i>, &amp; USA <i>(<a href="/wiki/Miami" title="Miami">Miami</a>)</i>.</li>
      </ul> 
      <p>Other national companies with an air operator certification: </p> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r998391716">.mw-parser-output .div-col{margin-top:0.3em;column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .div-col-small{font-size:90%}.mw-parser-output .div-col-rules{column-rule:1px solid #aaa}.mw-parser-output .div-col dl,.mw-parser-output .div-col ol,.mw-parser-output .div-col ul{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .div-col li,.mw-parser-output .div-col dd{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}</style>
      <div class="div-col" style="column-width: 30em;"> 
       <ul>
        <li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Aero_Club_Suriname&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Aero Club Suriname (page does not exist)">Aero Club Suriname</a> <i>(ACS)</i> – General Aviation Aeroclub</li> 
        <li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Coronie_Aero_Farmers&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Coronie Aero Farmers (page does not exist)">Coronie Aero Farmers</a> <i>(CAF)</i> – Agriculture Cropdusting</li> 
        <li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eagle_Air_Services&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Eagle Air Services (page does not exist)">Eagle Air Services</a> <i>(EAS)</i> – Agriculture Cropdusting</li> 
        <li><a href="/w/index.php?title=ERK_Farms&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="ERK Farms (page does not exist)">ERK Farms</a> <i>(ERK)</i> – Agriculture Cropdusting</li> 
        <li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Overeem_Air_Service&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Overeem Air Service (page does not exist)">Overeem Air Service</a> <i>(OAS)</i> – General Aviation Charters</li> 
        <li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pegasus_Air_Service&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Pegasus Air Service (page does not exist)">Pegasus Air Service</a> <i>(PAS)</i> – Helicopter Charters</li> 
        <li><a href="/wiki/Military_of_Suriname" class="mw-redirect" title="Military of Suriname">Suriname Air Force / Surinaamse Luchtmacht</a> <i>(SAF / LUMA)</i> – Military Aviation Surinam Air Force</li> 
        <li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Surinam_Sky_Farmers&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Surinam Sky Farmers (page does not exist)">Surinam Sky Farmers</a> <i>(SSF)</i> – Agriculture Cropdusting</li> 
        <li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Surinaamse_Medische_Zendings_Vliegdienst&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Surinaamse Medische Zendings Vliegdienst (page does not exist)">Surinaamse Medische Zendings Vliegdienst</a> <i>(MAF – Mission Aviation Fellowship)</i> – General Aviation Missionary</li> 
        <li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Vortex_Aviation_Suriname&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Vortex Aviation Suriname (page does not exist)">Vortex Aviation Suriname</a> <i>(VAS)</i> – General Aviation Maintenance &amp; Flightschool</li>
       </ul> 
      </div> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suriname&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Suriname" title="Health in Suriname">Health in Suriname</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Global_Burden_of_Disease" class="mw-redirect" title="Global Burden of Disease">Global Burden of Disease</a> Study provides an on-line data source for analyzing updated estimates of health for 359 diseases and injuries and 84 risk factors from 1990 to 2017 in most of the world's countries.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[84]</a></sup> Comparing Suriname with other Caribbean nations show that in 2017 the age-standardized <a href="/wiki/Death_rate" class="mw-redirect" title="Death rate">death rate</a> for all causes was 793 (males 969, females 641) per 100,000, far below the 1219 of <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a>, somewhat below the 944 of <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a> but considerably above the 424 of <a href="/wiki/Bermuda" title="Bermuda">Bermuda</a>. In 1990 the death rate was 960 per 100,000. <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">Life expectancy</a> in 2017 was 72 years (males 69, females 75). The death rate for children &lt; 5 years was 581 per 100,000 compared to 1308 in Haiti and 102 in Bermuda. In 1990 and 2017, leading causes of age-standardized death rates were cardiovascular disease, cancer and diabetes/chronic kidney disease. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suriname&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Suriname" title="Education in Suriname">Education in Suriname</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Education in Suriname is compulsory until the age of 12,<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[85]</a></sup> and the nation had a net primary enrollment rate of 94% in 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-hdrstats.undp.org_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hdrstats.undp.org-89">[86]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Literacy" title="Literacy">Literacy</a> is very common, particularly among men.<sup id="cite_ref-hdrstats.undp.org_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hdrstats.undp.org-89">[86]</a></sup> The main university in the country is the <a href="/wiki/Anton_de_Kom_University_of_Suriname" title="Anton de Kom University of Suriname">Anton de Kom University of Suriname</a>. </p>
      <p>From elementary school to high school there are 13 grades. The elementary school has six grades, middle school four grades and high school three grades. Students take a test in the end of elementary school to determine whether they will go to the MULO (secondary modern school) or a middle school of lower standards like LBO. Students from the elementary school wear a green shirt with jeans, while middle school students wear a blue shirt with jeans. </p>
      <p>Students going from the second grade of middle school to the third grade have to choose between the business or science courses. This will determine what their major subjects will be. In order to go on to study math and physics, the student must have a total of 12 points. If the student has fewer points, he/she will go into the business courses or fail the grade.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity">Biodiversity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suriname&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Biodiversity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Dendrobates_azureus_(Dendrobates_tinctorius)_Edit.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Dendrobates_azureus_%28Dendrobates_tinctorius%29_Edit.jpg/220px-Dendrobates_azureus_%28Dendrobates_tinctorius%29_Edit.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Dendrobates_azureus_%28Dendrobates_tinctorius%29_Edit.jpg/330px-Dendrobates_azureus_%28Dendrobates_tinctorius%29_Edit.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Dendrobates_azureus_%28Dendrobates_tinctorius%29_Edit.jpg/440px-Dendrobates_azureus_%28Dendrobates_tinctorius%29_Edit.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2591" data-file-height="2002"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Dendrobates_azureus_(Dendrobates_tinctorius)_Edit.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Blue_poison_dart_frog" title="Blue poison dart frog">blue poison dart frog</a> is endemic to Suriname.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity_in_Suriname" title="Biodiversity in Suriname">Biodiversity in Suriname</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Due to the variety of habitats and temperatures, biodiversity in Suriname is considered high.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[87]</a></sup> In October 2013, 16 international scientists researching the ecosystems during a three-week expedition in Suriname's Upper Palumeu River Watershed catalogued 1,378 species and found 60—including six frogs, one snake, and 11 fish—that may be previously unknown species.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[88]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[89]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[90]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[91]</a></sup> According to the environmental non-profit <a href="/wiki/Conservation_International" title="Conservation International">Conservation International</a>, which funded the expedition, Suriname's ample supply of fresh water is vital to the biodiversity and healthy ecosystems of the region.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[92]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Snakewood (<i><a href="/wiki/Brosimum_guianense" title="Brosimum guianense">Brosimum guianense</a></i>), a tree, is native to this tropical region of the Americas. Customs in Suriname report that snakewood is often illegally exported to French Guiana, thought to be for the crafts industry.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[93]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_preservation">Environmental preservation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suriname&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Environmental preservation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>On 21 March 2013, Suriname's REDD+ Readiness Preparation Proposal (R-PP 2013) was approved by the member countries of the Participants Committee of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Forest_Carbon_Partnership_Facility&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Forest Carbon Partnership Facility (page does not exist)">Forest Carbon Partnership Facility</a> (FCPF).<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[94]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As in other parts of Central and South America, indigenous communities have increased their activism to protect their lands and preserve habitat. In March 2015, the "<a href="/wiki/Trio_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Trio people">Trio</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wayana_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Wayana people">Wayana</a> communities presented a declaration of cooperation to the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Suriname" class="mw-redirect" title="National Assembly of Suriname">National Assembly of Suriname</a> that announces an indigenous conservation corridor spanning 72,000 square kilometers (27,799 square miles) of southern Suriname. The declaration, led by these indigenous communities and with the support of <a href="/wiki/Conservation_International" title="Conservation International">Conservation International</a> (CI) and <a href="/wiki/World_Wildlife_Fund" class="mw-redirect" title="World Wildlife Fund">World Wildlife Fund</a> <a href="/wiki/WWF_Guianas" title="WWF Guianas">(WWF) Guianas</a>, comprises almost half of the total area of Suriname."<sup id="cite_ref-guardians_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardians-98">[95]</a></sup> This area includes large forests and is considered "essential for the country's <a href="/wiki/Climate_resilience" title="Climate resilience">climate resilience</a>, freshwater security, and green development strategy."<sup id="cite_ref-guardians_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardians-98">[95]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suriname&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>Traditionally, <i><a href="/wiki/De_Ware_Tijd" title="De Ware Tijd">De Ware Tijd</a></i> was the major newspaper of the country, but since the '90s <i><a href="/wiki/Times_of_Suriname" title="Times of Suriname">Times of Suriname</a>, <a href="/wiki/De_West" title="De West">De West</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Dagblad_Suriname" title="Dagblad Suriname">Dagblad Suriname</a></i> have also been well-read newspapers; all publish primarily in Dutch.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[96]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Suriname has twenty-four radio stations, most of them also broadcast through the Internet. There are twelve television sources: <a href="/wiki/Ampie%27s_Broadcasting_Corporation" title="Ampie's Broadcasting Corporation">ABC</a> (Ch. 4–1, 2), RBN (Ch. 5–1, 2), Rasonic TV (Ch. 7), STVS (Ch. 8–1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6), Apintie (Ch. 10–1), ATV (Ch. 12–1, 2, 3, 4), Radika (Ch. 14), SCCN (Ch. 17–1, 2, 3), Pipel TV (Ch. 18–1, 2), Trishul (Ch. 20–1, 2, 3, 4), Garuda (Ch. 23–1, 2, 3), Sangeetmala (Ch. 26), Ch. 30, Ch. 31, Ch.32, Ch.38, SCTV (Ch. 45). Also listened to is <a href="/wiki/Mart_(broadcaster)" title="Mart (broadcaster)">mArt</a>, a broadcaster from Amsterdam founded by people from Suriname. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kondreman&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Kondreman (page does not exist)">Kondreman</a> is one of the popular cartoons in Suriname. </p>
      <p>There are also three major news sites: Starnieuws, Suriname Herald and GFC Nieuws. </p>
      <p>In 2012, Suriname was ranked joint 22nd with Japan in the worldwide Press Freedom Index by the organization <a href="/wiki/Reporters_Without_Borders" title="Reporters Without Borders">Reporters Without Borders</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[97]</a></sup> This was ahead of the US (47th), the UK (28th), and France (38th). </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suriname&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Amazon_jungle_from_above.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Amazon_jungle_from_above.jpg/220px-Amazon_jungle_from_above.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Amazon_jungle_from_above.jpg/330px-Amazon_jungle_from_above.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Amazon_jungle_from_above.jpg/440px-Amazon_jungle_from_above.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1071"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Amazon_jungle_from_above.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Central_Suriname_Nature_Reserve" title="Central Suriname Nature Reserve">Central Suriname Nature Reserve</a> seen from the Voltzberg
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Most tourists visit Suriname for the <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">biodiversity</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_Basin" class="mw-redirect" title="Amazon Basin">Amazonian</a> rain forests in the south of the country, which are noted for their flora and fauna. The <a href="/wiki/Central_Suriname_Nature_Reserve" title="Central Suriname Nature Reserve">Central Suriname Nature Reserve</a> is the biggest and one of the most popular reserves, along with the <a href="/wiki/Brownsberg_Nature_Park" title="Brownsberg Nature Park">Brownsberg Nature Park</a> which overlooks the <a href="/wiki/Brokopondo_Reservoir" title="Brokopondo Reservoir">Brokopondo Reservoir</a>, one of the largest man-made lakes in the world. In 2008, the <a href="/wiki/Berg_en_Dal_(Suriname)" class="mw-redirect" title="Berg en Dal (Suriname)">Berg en Dal Eco &amp; Cultural Resort</a> opened in Brokopondo.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[98]</a></sup> Tonka Island in the reservoir is home to a rustic <a href="/wiki/Eco-tourism" class="mw-redirect" title="Eco-tourism">eco-tourism</a> project run by the Saramaccaner Maroons.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[99]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pangi_(Maroon)" title="Pangi (Maroon)">Pangi</a> wraps and bowls made of calabashes are the two main products manufactured for tourists. The Maroons have learned that colorful and ornate pangis are popular with tourists.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[100]</a></sup> Other popular decorative souvenirs are hand-carved purple-hardwood made into bowls, plates, canes, wooden boxes, and wall decors. </p>
      <p>There are also many waterfalls throughout the country. Raleighvallen, or Raleigh Falls, is a 56,000-hectare (140,000-acre) nature reserve on the <a href="/wiki/Coppename_River" title="Coppename River">Coppename River</a>, rich in bird life. Also are the <a href="/wiki/Blanche_Marie_Falls" title="Blanche Marie Falls">Blanche Marie Falls</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Nickerie_River" title="Nickerie River">Nickerie River</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Wonotobo_Falls" title="Wonotobo Falls">Wonotobo Falls</a>. <a href="/wiki/Tafelberg,_Suriname" title="Tafelberg, Suriname">Tafelberg Mountain</a> in the centre of the country is surrounded by its own reserve – the <a href="/wiki/Tafelberg_Nature_Reserve" class="mw-redirect" title="Tafelberg Nature Reserve">Tafelberg Nature Reserve</a> – around the source of the <a href="/wiki/Saramacca_River" title="Saramacca River">Saramacca River</a>, as is the Voltzberg Nature Reserve further north on the Coppename River at Raleighvallen. In the interior are many <a href="/wiki/Maroon_(people)" class="mw-redirect" title="Maroon (people)">Maroon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Amerindian" class="mw-redirect" title="Amerindian">Amerindian</a> villages, many of which have their own reserves that are generally open to visitors. </p>
      <p>Suriname is one of the few countries in the world where at least one of each <a href="/wiki/Biome" title="Biome">biome</a> that the state possesses has been declared a wildlife reserve. Around 30% of the total land area of Suriname is protected by law as reserves. </p>
      <p>Other attractions include plantations such as <a href="/wiki/Laarwijk" title="Laarwijk">Laarwijk</a>, which is situated along the Suriname River. This plantation can be reached only by boat via Domburg, in the north central <a href="/wiki/Wanica_District" title="Wanica District">Wanica District</a> of Suriname. </p>
      <p>Crime rates continue to rise in Paramaribo and armed robberies are not uncommon. According to the current U.S. Department of State Travel Advisory at the date of the 2018 report's publication, Suriname has been assessed as Level 1: exercise normal precautions.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">[101]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Landmarks">Landmarks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suriname&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Landmarks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Cathedral_Paramaribo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Cathedral_Paramaribo.jpg/170px-Cathedral_Paramaribo.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="239" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Cathedral_Paramaribo.jpg/255px-Cathedral_Paramaribo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Cathedral_Paramaribo.jpg/340px-Cathedral_Paramaribo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="390" data-file-height="549"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Cathedral_Paramaribo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Saint_Peter_and_Paul_Cathedral,_Paramaribo" title="Saint Peter and Paul Cathedral, Paramaribo">Cathedral of St. Peter and Paul</a> in Paramaribo
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Jules_Wijdenbosch_Bridge" title="Jules Wijdenbosch Bridge">Jules Wijdenbosch Bridge</a> is a bridge over the river Suriname between Paramaribo and Meerzorg in the Commewijne district. The bridge was built during the tenure of President <a href="/wiki/Jules_Albert_Wijdenbosch" class="mw-redirect" title="Jules Albert Wijdenbosch">Jules Albert Wijdenbosch</a> (1996–2000) and was completed in 2000. The bridge is 52 metres (171&nbsp;ft) high, and 1,504 metres (4,934&nbsp;ft) long. It connects Paramaribo with Commewijne, a connection which previously could only be made by ferry. The purpose of the bridge was to facilitate and promote the development of the eastern part of Suriname. The bridge consists of two lanes (one lane each way) and is not accessible to pedestrians. </p>
      <p>The construction of the <a href="/wiki/Saint_Peter_and_Paul_Cathedral,_Paramaribo" title="Saint Peter and Paul Cathedral, Paramaribo">Sts. Peter and Paul Cathedral</a> started on 13 January 1883. Before it became a cathedral it was a theatre. The theatre was built in 1809 and burned down in 1820. </p>
      <p>Suriname is one of the few countries in the world where <a href="/wiki/Neveh_Shalom_Synagogue" title="Neveh Shalom Synagogue">a synagogue</a> is located next to <a href="/wiki/Mosque_Keizerstraat" title="Mosque Keizerstraat">a mosque</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[102]</a></sup> The two buildings are located next to each other in the centre of Paramaribo and have been known to share a parking facility during their respective religious rites, should they happen to coincide with one another. </p>
      <p>A relatively new landmark is the Hindu <a href="/wiki/Arya_Dewaker" title="Arya Dewaker">Arya Dewaker</a> temple in the Johan Adolf Pengelstraat in <a href="/wiki/Wanica" class="mw-redirect" title="Wanica">Wanica</a>, Paramaribo, which was inaugurated in 2001. A special characteristic of the temple is that it does not have images of the Hindu divinities, as they are forbidden in the <a href="/wiki/Arya_Samaj" title="Arya Samaj">Arya Samaj</a>, the Hindu movement to which the people who built the temple belong. Instead, the building is covered by many texts derived from the Vedas and other Hindu scriptures. The beautiful architecture makes the temple a tourist attraction. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suriname&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r936637989">.mw-parser-output .portal{border:solid #aaa 1px;padding:0}.mw-parser-output .portal.tleft{margin:0.5em 1em 0.5em 0}.mw-parser-output .portal.tright{margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul{display:table;box-sizing:border-box;padding:0.1em;max-width:175px;background:#f9f9f9;font-size:85%;line-height:110%;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul>li{display:table-row}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul>li>span:first-child{display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul>li>span:last-child{display:table-cell;padding:0.2em 0.2em 0.2em 0.3em;vertical-align:middle}</style>
      <div role="navigation" aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright"> 
       <ul> 
        <li><span><img alt="flag" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Flag_of_Suriname.svg/32px-Flag_of_Suriname.svg.png" decoding="async" width="32" height="21" class="noviewer thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Flag_of_Suriname.svg/48px-Flag_of_Suriname.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Flag_of_Suriname.svg/64px-Flag_of_Suriname.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600"></span><span><a href="/wiki/Portal:Suriname" title="Portal:Suriname">Suriname portal</a></span></li>

      <div style="clear:both;"></div> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Suriname&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style>
      <div class="reflist"> 
       <div class="mw-references-wrap">
        <ol class="references"> 
         <li id="cite_note-13"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-13">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Both <a href="/wiki/French_Guiana" title="French Guiana">French Guiana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Falkland_Islands" title="Falkland Islands">Falkland Islands</a> are less extensive and populous, but they are an <a href="/wiki/Overseas_department" class="mw-redirect" title="Overseas department">overseas department</a> and <a href="/wiki/Overseas_region" class="mw-redirect" title="Overseas region">region</a> of France and an <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Territory" class="mw-redirect" title="British Overseas Territory">overseas territory</a> of the United Kingdom respectively.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-15"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-15">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Suriname has been carbon negative since at least 2014.</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-68"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-68">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The <a href="/wiki/International_Organization_for_Migration" title="International Organization for Migration">International Organization for Migration</a> made a confusion regarding the number of Surinamese migrants living in French Guiana. Their number is already included in the number for France (24,753 at the time of writing), as can be seen here: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.insee.fr/fr/statistiques/3633212#tableau-Econtinent_radio1">données complémentaires</a>.</span> </li> 
        </ol>
       </div>
      </div>
